Important News

137th Meeting of the Legislative Yuan

Passed the Law on Disciplinary Actions for Public Officials

The Legislative Yuan held its 137th meeting on the 28th. Thirty-four members, including Liu Guanxun, were present, with Shao Yuanchong presiding. The following items were discussed: (1) The International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea and its attached regulations were decided to be submitted to the Foreign Affairs and Military Affairs Committees for review. (2) The report of the Legislative Yuan's Legal System Committee on the interpretation of Articles 7 and 13 of the Publications Law was decided to be passed according to the review report. (3) The report of the Legislative Yuan's Legal System Committee on the draft Law on the Organization of the Public Officials Disciplinary Committee was decided to be passed. (4) The draft Law on Disciplinary Actions for Public Officials was reviewed and decided to be passed with amendments. (5) The draft amendments to the County Organization Law were reviewed. (6) The draft amendments to the Implementing Regulations of the County Organization Law were reviewed. It was decided that the above two cases should be submitted to the Legal System Committee for joint review with the Autonomous Law Drafting Committee.

Legislative Yuan's Interpretation of the Publications Law

The Central Propaganda Department previously stated that the registration of newspapers and news agencies was handled by the Party Headquarters, while the filing of cases was handled by administrative agencies. After the promulgation of the Publications Law, many provinces have had doubts about handling the above-mentioned matters. Before the promulgation of the Publications Law, local governments had their own provisional regulations for handling newspaper and news agency matters. Article 7 of the Publications Law has provisions for registration. Does the registration mentioned in this article equate to filing a case? And should the previous case-filing procedures in various places be uniformly suspended because of this registration? Regarding the coordination procedures between the government and the Party Headquarters for newspaper registration, should publications concerning Party affairs and Party doctrines be registered with both the Party Headquarters and the government? Furthermore, what is the scope of the matters designated in Articles 7 and 13 regarding the recording of Party doctrines and Party affairs? Can the publication of resolutions of the Central Standing Committee by newspapers be regarded as a record of Party affairs? The Legislative Yuan was consulted for interpretation. The Water Court issued it to the Legal System Committee for review. The committee's review concluded that the filing of cases and registration of newspapers and news agencies serve the same purpose: to know their internal organization and the purpose of their publication before they begin publishing, so as to facilitate inspection and verification. After the implementation of the Publications Law, there is no need to fulfill the case-filing procedures in addition to applying for registration in accordance with the law. All kinds of provisional regulations originally stipulated by local governments regarding this case-filing matter should uniformly become invalid. Newspapers or magazines that publish matters related to Party doctrines or Party affairs should apply for registration with both the Party Headquarters and the government. Articles 7 and 27 of the Publications Law stipulate this very clearly. The resolutions of the Central Standing Committee are naturally matters related to Party doctrines or Party affairs. The publication of such resolutions should be subject to the provisions of Article 7, Paragraph 3, and Article 13, Paragraph 2, of the Publications Law. This opinion was submitted in a report requesting immediate delivery to the plenary session. Today (the 28th), the 137th meeting of the Legislative Yuan has decided to pass it according to the review report.

Law on Disciplinary Actions for Public Officials

The Legislative Yuan's 137th meeting on the 28th passed the Law on Disciplinary Actions for Public Officials with amendments, as follows:

Chapter I General Provisions (Article 1) Public officials shall not be subject to disciplinary action except in accordance with this law, unless otherwise provided by law. (Article 2) Public officials who have committed any of the following acts shall be subject to disciplinary action:

Chapter II Disciplinary Sanctions (Article 3) Disciplinary sanctions shall be as follows: 1. Dismissal; 2. Demotion; 3. Salary Reduction; 4. Demerit; 5. Reprimand. The sanctions in items 2 to 4 of the preceding paragraph shall not apply to political appointees. (Article 4) Dismissal shall, in addition to dismissal from the current position, also suspend re-employment for a certain period. The period of suspension of re-employment in the preceding paragraph shall be at least one year. (Article 5) Demotion shall be a reduction of one or two grades in the current official rank, with a change of rank. No promotion shall be allowed for two years from the date of the change of rank. Those who are demoted and have no rank to demote shall have their monthly salary reduced by the difference between each grade, for a period of two years. (Article 6) Salary reduction shall be a reduction of 10% or 20% of the current monthly salary, for a period of one month to one year. (Article 7) Those who receive a demerit shall not be promoted within one year from the date of the demerit. Those who receive three demerits within one year shall have their salary reduced by the superior officer in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article. (Article 8) Reprimands shall be made in writing or verbally. (Article 9) Disciplinary sanctions decided by the Central Public Officials Disciplinary Committee shall be reported to the Judicial Yuan, along with three copies of the decision, within seven days after the decision. If the disciplined person is of the recommended rank or above, the Judicial Yuan shall submit it to the National Government or notify their superior officer to carry it out. If the disciplined person is of the appointed rank, the Judicial Yuan shall notify their superior officer to carry it out. The Ministry of Personnel shall be notified in all cases. Disciplinary sanctions decided by the local Public Officials Disciplinary Committee shall be notified to the superior officer of the disciplined person along with the decision within seven days after the decision, and shall be reported to the Judicial Yuan and the Ministry of Personnel at the same time.

Chapter III Disciplinary Agencies (Article 10) If the Control Yuan believes that a public official has committed any of the acts specified in Article 2 and should be subject to disciplinary action, it shall transfer the impeachment case along with the evidence to the disciplinary agency in accordance with the following provisions: 1. If the impeached person is a member of the National Government Committee, it shall be sent to the Supervisory Committee of the Central Party Headquarters. 2. If the impeached person is a political appointee other than those in the preceding item, it shall be sent to the National Government. 3. If the impeached person is an administrative official, it shall be sent to the Public Officials Disciplinary Committee. (Article 11) If the heads of various Yuan, Ministries, and Commissions, or the highest local administrative officer, believe that a public official under their jurisdiction has committed any of the acts specified in Article 2, they shall prepare a document stating the reasons and forward it along with the evidence to the Control Yuan for review. However, for public officials under the recommended rank under their jurisdiction, they may directly send it to the Public Officials Disciplinary Committee for review. (Article 12) Demerits or reprimands for public officials of the recommended rank or below may be directly carried out by the chief officer. Chapter IV Disciplinary Procedures (Article 13) The disciplinary agency shall, when necessary,

Page 10

designate a committee member to investigate the disciplinary case transferred to it. (Article 14) In addition to conducting its own investigation according to its authority, the disciplinary agency may entrust administrative or judicial agencies to investigate the transferred case. (Article 15) The disciplinary agency shall send a copy of the original documents to the person subject to disciplinary action and designate a period for them to submit a statement of defense. When necessary, they may also order them to appear in court for questioning. If the person subject to disciplinary action fails to submit a statement of defense or fails to appear in court as ordered within the designated period, the disciplinary agency may directly make a decision on the disciplinary action. (Article 16) If the disciplinary agency believes that the circumstances of the transferred disciplinary case are serious, it may notify the relevant superior officer to suspend the duties of the person subject to disciplinary action in advance. If the superior officer believes that the circumstances are serious when submitting a request to the Control Yuan for review or to the Public Officials Disciplinary Committee for review in accordance with the provisions of Article 11, they may also suspend the duties of the public official under their jurisdiction in advance according to their authority. Public officials whose duties have been suspended in accordance with the preceding two paragraphs shall be allowed to resume their duties and shall be compensated for their salary during the period of suspension if they have not been dismissed or sentenced to criminal punishment. (Article 17) The duties of a public official shall be automatically suspended in any of the following circumstances: 1. They are detained during the criminal litigation procedure. 2. They are declared to be deprived of their civil rights in accordance with a final criminal judgment. 3. They are sentenced to detention or more in accordance with a final criminal judgment and are serving the sentence. (Article 18) The performance of official duties by a public official whose duties have been suspended in accordance with the preceding two articles shall be invalid. (Article 19) The provisions of the Criminal Procedure Law regarding the recusal of judges shall apply mutatis mutandis to the recusal of members of the Public Officials Disciplinary Committee. (Article 20) The decision of the disciplinary agency shall be made with the consent of more than half of the members present. If the opinions of the members present are divided into three or more views and cannot obtain the consent of more than half, the views shall be arranged in order from the most unfavorable to the person subject to disciplinary action, and the next most unfavorable view shall be included until the number of people reaches more than half. (Article 21) The decision of the disciplinary agency shall be made in the form of a written decision, which shall be signed by all members present. The written decision shall be sent by the disciplinary agency to the person subject to disciplinary action, notified to the Control Yuan and the government agency to which the person subject to disciplinary action belongs, and published in the National Government Gazette or the Provincial Government Gazette.

Chapter V Relationship between Disciplinary Sanctions and Criminal Judgments (Article 22) If the disciplinary agency believes that a disciplinary case involves criminal suspicion, it shall immediately transfer it to the relevant court for trial. (Article 23) The disciplinary procedure shall not be commenced if the same act is already under criminal investigation or trial. (Article 24) When a criminal litigation procedure is commenced during a disciplinary procedure for the same act, the disciplinary procedure shall be suspended until a final criminal judgment is made. (Article 25) A disciplinary sanction may still be imposed even if the same act has already been dismissed, exempted, or acquitted. (Article 26) A disciplinary sanction may still be imposed even if the same act has been sentenced to criminal punishment but has not been deprived of civil rights.

Chapter VI Supplementary Provisions (Article 27) Acts that should be subject to disciplinary action, even if they occurred before the implementation of this law, may be subject to disciplinary action in accordance with this law. (Article 28) This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

National Government Promulgates the Customs Duty Short-Term Treasury Bond Regulations

The original text of the Regulations on the Customs Duty Short-Term Treasury Bonds of the Republic of China, promulgated by the National Government on the 28th of the month, is as follows: (Article 1) These treasury bonds are named the Customs Duty Short-Term Treasury Bonds of the Republic of China in the 20th year to be used for circulating the national treasury. (Article 2) The fixed amount of these treasury bonds is 80 million yuan. (Article 3) These treasury bonds will be issued on April 1, 1931. (Article 4) The interest rate of these treasury bonds is fixed at eight li per month. (Article 5) The principal and interest of these treasury bonds shall be repaid monthly from April 1931, with the interest decreasing as the principal is repaid, divided equally over 100 months (i.e., one yuan of principal per hundred yuan per month). The total amount of principal and interest shall be paid off by the end of July 1939. (Article 6) The principal and interest to be repaid for these treasury bonds shall be allocated in full from the increased revenue of customs duties as designated by the Ministry of Finance, specifically ordering the Inspector General of Customs to allocate the amount published on the repayment schedule each month and deposit it with the Central Bank, which shall also serve as the custodian for the Fund Management Committee, for the purpose of safekeeping and payment of principal and interest when due. (Article 7) The repayment of principal and interest for these treasury bonds shall be handled by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, designated by the Ministry of Finance as the paying agents. (Article 8) These treasury bonds shall be issued at 98 per cent of face value, i.e., 98 silver dollars shall be actually received for each 100 yuan of face value. (Article 9) These treasury bonds are designated as unregistered. (Article 10) These treasury bonds are designated in denominations of 5,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, 100 yuan, and 10 yuan. (Article 11) These treasury bonds may be mortgaged and traded at will and may be used as collateral when security deposits must be paid on official business. (Article 12) These treasury bonds may be used as the guarantee reserve of banks. (Article 13) Any act of counterfeiting these bonds or damaging their credit shall be punished by the judicial authorities in accordance with the law. (Article 14) These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Hanyang Aircraft Team Disaster in Reconnaissance Mission

Two Planes Collide in Tuanfeng, Killing Two Pilots

First and Fourth Teams Hold Memorial Service in Hankou

HANKOU COMMUNICATION: The First and Fourth Aircraft Teams of the Aviation Administration of the Ministry of Military Affairs stationed in Hankou were dispatched to Luoshan on the 24th of this month to scout for bandits. Five aircraft, numbers 41, 42, 43, 44, and 45, were jointly dispatched, with pilots from both teams co-piloting. As they flew to the Tuanfeng area under the jurisdiction of Huanggang County, the air bag of the fourth aircraft (number 44) was lowered to the ground to exchange air. Unexpectedly, the fifth aircraft (number 45), which was flying straight forward, was unable to avoid it, causing the two aircraft to collide. Because aircraft 44 was exchanging air and lacked horsepower, it crashed into the wilderness near Tuanfeng. The machine was damaged, and gasoline leaked out, causing a fire. The pilots driving the aircraft, Zhang Mu and Liu Zhengxin, were paralyzed and unable to move from the high fall and were immediately burned to death by the fire. The fuselage was also destroyed by the fire. Aircraft 45 was also severely damaged due to the collision. While in a state of crisis, aircraft 43, which was ahead, heard the alarm and rushed back to help, fortunately without encountering danger. The pilot was unharmed, but the aircraft was severely damaged and could not be repaired. It has been verified that the horsepower of these two aircraft was over 300 horsepower, and they had only been flying for over a year. Each aircraft was worth approximately 150,000 yuan. The two pilots who died, Zhang Mu, was from Xianyou County, Fujian Province, was 24 years old, and graduated from Guangdong Aviation School, serving as a pilot in the Fourth Team. Liu Zhengxin, from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province, was 21 years old and also graduated from Guangdong Aviation School, serving as a pilot in the First Team. Neither had family members in Hankou. Afterwards, the two teams telegraphed their families and submitted a report to the Ministry of Military Affairs for generous condolences. All officers and soldiers of the two teams wore black armbands from the 25th to express their condolences. A public memorial service was held at 10 a.m. on the 27th to express their condolences, presided over by Yan Yucong, the captain of the First Team. Dozens of people from the aviation community attended the memorial service, and the situation was extremely sad. This is also an unfortunate event for our aviation community (March 27th).

Han Fuqu Supervises the Suppression of Bandits in Baodugu

Planned to Clear the Bandit Nest Within One Month

JINAN COMMUNICATION: Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, has decided to clear the bandit nest in Baodugu. He has ordered the Third Route Army under his command to join forces with the troops of Chen Yaohan in Yizhou, Wang Jun in Mengyin County, and Ma Hongkui in Tai'an to encircle the area. Han himself went south to supervise the troops and severely suppress the bandits.

The pistol brigade under Lei Taiping served as the guard. Lei Taiping took the brigade headquarters and the special service battalion by train to Qufu last night (the 25th). This morning (the 26th), a special train was prepared on the Jinpu Railway, consisting of 14 covered wagons, two flat cars, one factory car, and one guard car, and four cars and the Tiejiache North-China took the lead. At one o'clock in the afternoon, the staff of the accompanying agencies boarded the train, including Li Tianni, Director of the Inspection Department of the Provincial Government, Zhao Liantang, Deputy Director, Jiang Cuijing and Chen Yunqi, Secretaries, Li Tingwei of the Department of Agriculture and Mining, Wang Guangrui of the Finance Department, Zhou Yanguang of the Education Department, Chen Ganru of the Civil Affairs Department, Ren Youwu, Clerk of the High Court, Huang Jie, Officer of the Propaganda Section of the Provincial Party Headquarters, Meng Guangshan, Adjutant of the Headquarters, and Liu Shuxiang, Chief of the Staff Office. In addition, there were two squads of soldiers from the First Battalion of the pistol brigade. At one thirty, Han and the people who came to see him off arrived at the station and said to the press that all the armies engaged in bandit suppression would arrive at their destinations and the general attack order had not yet been issued. There were no more than 3,000 bandits in Baodugu, and they were divided into several groups that were not under unified command. It was expected that the bandit nest could be cleared within a month. He would first go to Qufu, then inspect the counties along the way through Sishui, Mengyin, Yishui, Feixian, Tengxian, Zouxian, Wenshang, Yanzhou, and Tai'an and returned to Jinan in about 20 days. The train left Jinan at around 2 pm. It was heard that Han had printed hundreds of proclamations to be posted in the bandit suppression area. The text of the proclamation was as follows: "Since the rise of the revolutionary army and the spread of war in various provinces, the suffering of the people has been unprecedented. The bandits in various places have taken advantage of the opportunity to rise up and plunder, so that even after the military affairs have been settled, the elders and brothers are still displaced and cannot live in peace. Even their houses are in ruins and their fields are abandoned. It is extremely heartbreaking to talk about it. Since the Chairman took over the military and civilian affairs of the province, he has consistently adhered to the principle of using the army to protect the people and ensuring the people's security as the army's responsibility. He deeply knows that the reason why the people are not at ease is that the bandits have not been quelled. Therefore, he has repeatedly ordered the divisions and brigades under his command and the local militia groups to severely suppress all the bandits within the territory, in order to allow the elders and brothers to live and work in peace. Although troops have been dispatched to suppress the bandits, the bandits often leave when the troops arrive and return when the troops leave, and the root cause has not been eradicated. The bandits in the areas bordering Teng, Fei, and Mengyin counties are especially cunning, and the people have suffered the most. Every time I think about it, it is difficult for me to sleep and eat. The people and the bandits cannot coexist. If there are bandits, there will be no people; if there are people, there must be no bandits. In view of the past failures in bandit suppression, the Chairman has led a strong force to supervise the suppression and vowed to sweep away the nests and eliminate this major scourge for the people. Do not disturb each other when the army passes. If bandits should try to escape, it is hoped that the elders and brothers will cooperate to block them or send them to the government for punishment in accordance with the law, so that none will escape the net. From now on, fathers, elders, brothers, and sisters will be able to emerge from the water and fire and ascend to the mat, so that they can share the happiness of peace. I am afraid that the people of all circles may not know this, so I hereby issue this proclamation." (26th)

The Haiyuan Pavilion Collection of Books is Priced at One Million

Yang Jingfu Expresses His Willingness to Donate Half and Sell Half

The Government Will Send Personnel to Tianjin to Negotiate

JINAN COMMUNICATION: The collection of books of the Yang family of Haiyuan Pavilion in Liaocheng was previously investigated by the Shandong Provincial Government upon consultation with the Ministry of Education, and its sale was prohibited. The Education Department then instructed the Shandong Library to conduct an investigation. Subsequently, the library drafted a draft agreement on the Haiyuan Pavilion collection of books (which was published in a previous newspaper) and sought the written consent of the Yang family. Yang Jingfu, the owner of the collection, replied to the library after receiving the draft in Tianjin, saying that he was "grateful for the repeated expressions of concern, but would reply to the draft agreement in detail later." However, to this day, there has been no written reply. Only a few days ago, Yang Jingfu came to Jinan once and indirectly expressed his willingness to accept the third method of the agreement (i.e., the government prepares a price to purchase the entire collection). Later, after being persuaded by relatives and friends that this would damage the family's reputation, Yang expressed his willingness to accept the second method (i.e., donate half and sell half), but the government must offer a price of one million yuan. Upon receiving this news, the government immediately sent personnel to negotiate, but Yang had already returned to Tianjin. The matter now rests on Yang Jingfu's decision with his wife's father, Lao Zhichang, while Yang's old lady (Yang Jingfu's adoptive mother) is no longer able to make a decision. Therefore, the government plans to send personnel to Tianjin to negotiate with Yang Jingfu. Since Yang Jingfu has expressed his willingness to donate half and sell half, this problem should not be difficult to solve. However, the Shandong Provincial Treasury is currently extremely depleted, and it is feared that the source of the huge sum of money for the books will become a problem. According to a certain bibliophile, the books in the Yang family's collection in Jinan are not rare. If all the books stored in Tianjin were transported back, it would not be excessive to ask for one million yuan for half donation and half sale. According to reports, the Yang family's collection of books includes Yingshu Yulu, but several recently discovered works are not recorded in Yingshu Yulu. There is a Song edition of Zhuangzi, which Yang Jingfu sold to Zhou Shutao (son of the former Governor of Liangjiang, Zhou Fu) for 3,000 yuan, which is the most complete edition in China. There is also a Song edition of Shicai Hall Hanji, 30 volumes of the main collection and 10 volumes of the outer collection, for a total of 32 volumes, bound into four cases, which is also the only surviving copy in China. There is also Su Dongpo's handwritten and Tao poems, which those who have seen it say is still as complete as new. The above three works are not recorded in Yingshu Yulu. In addition, the Haiyuan Pavilion also has two copies of the Song Yaoben Hanji, which, although not the Shicai Hall edition, are also extremely precious. (26th)

Zhang Xueliang Promises to Allocate Military Expenses for the Jin Sui Army

1.5 Million Yuan Per Month

TAIYUAN COMMUNICATION: The Jin-Sui military expenditure issue has caused tension here since the Liaoning side telegraphed a few days ago, ordering Jin to raise the funds themselves. The price of Jin currency has also soared repeatedly, which is related to this. General Xu, Yang, Sun and others have repeatedly discussed and sent representatives to Shenyang to see Mr. Zhang, stating that Shanxi is unable to bear the burden and requesting Mr. Zhang to handle the matter in accordance with the Tianjin Resolution. The representative telegraphed back yesterday, saying that Mr. Zhang had expressed his approval of our request, but ordered Lian to report the Shanxi revenue and expenditure budget book immediately for verification, and ordered to reduce the military expenditure of each army as appropriate. According to another telegram, although Mr. Zhang agreed to assist the Jin-Sui military expenditure on a monthly basis, it should not exceed 1.5 million yuan per month. Moreover, this case was approved by Deputy Commander Zhang in both the Tianjin and Fan Yang meetings. Since the Jin army has been inspected and dispatched by the Northeast, the military expenditure should be subsidized by the Northeast. Recently, Deputy Commander Zhang ordered Jin and Sui provinces to raise the funds themselves. In fact, Shanxi's finances are unable to do so, so the military and political authorities still unanimously request Deputy Commander Zhang to handle the matter in accordance with the Tianjin Agreement. As for the exchange of banknotes for cash, the price of each yuan has risen from 2.4 yuan to 3 yuan in the past three to five days, and the people are in a state of extreme anxiety. However, many merchants are taking advantage of the situation to raise prices. Although the government has promised to do its best to maintain the provincial banknotes, the price of the banknotes is still falling. (24th)

Zhu Peide Departs from Xu to Bian

Xuzhou Dispatch: Zhu Peide's military inspection in Xuzhou concluded on the afternoon of the 25th. On the morning of the 26th, he gathered officers of the 7th Division at Jiulishan to review and give instructions. Before 9 o'clock, the division's direct units and the 19th and 21st Brigades, along with the 37th, 38th, 41st, and 42nd Regiments, comprising over 400 officers of the rank of warrant officer and above, assembled at the large parade ground. Then, after criticizing the inspection results, he delivered a speech, stating that the 7th Division had a long history in the revolution, fighting in various provinces since the campaign against Yuan Shikai. He said the division's achievements after a long war last year were generally acceptable, and he hoped they would work harder to train and permanently preserve their glorious history. After Zhu's speech, Wang Jun continued, mainly elaborating on Zhu's words to encourage them. The event concluded at 1 p.m. Zhu is scheduled to leave Xuzhou on the morning of the 27th and travel west. Along the way, he will inspect Du Run's 40th Regiment of the 7th Division in Dangshan before heading to Kaifeng. Wu Qingzhi, head of the First Inspection Class, along with the entire inspection committee, departed for Bian this morning. Notorious Bandit Jiang Guochang Killed in Eastern Anhui

Remnants of Ma Yuren's Band Fleeing Towards Jiangsu Border

Bengbu Dispatch: Jiang Guochang, a notorious bandit in eastern Anhui, nicknamed "Three Legs," has been harassing eastern Anhui for more than a decade. Recently, he colluded with the remnants of Ma Yuren's band, led by Qi Yaozong, and roamed between Jiangsu and Anhui. The National Army has repeatedly encircled and suppressed them, but they have not been completely eradicated. Earlier this month, near Xiaobian Village along the Jinpu Railway in Mingguang, they attempted to intercept trains. Zhang Lisheng, commander of the 2nd Cavalry Division, dispatched Ge Wucheng's 3rd Brigade and Zhang Shutian's 4th Brigade of the division, along with police and local militias from Chuzhou and Lai'an counties, to剿辦and pursue them. The bandits fled to the western border of Chuzhou County. On the 24th, the two cavalry brigades surrounded the bandits in villages such as Xiaoyangchong and Erwangzhuang and launched a fierce attack, killing over 400 bandits. Jiang Guochang and a pseudo-battalion commander under his command, surnamed Yang, were also killed on the spot. Over sixty bandits were captured alive, and over one hundred and forty male and female hostages were rescued. The officers and soldiers then cut off Jiang's head and transported it to Chuzhou County. Today (26th) at around 3 p.m., it was transferred to Bengbu, where it will be hung up for public display. With Jiang's death, a major scourge in eastern Anhui has been eliminated. Qi Yaozong's band, finding it difficult to establish a foothold in Anhui, has already fled east, intending to escape back to Jiangsu Province. Zhang Lisheng has telegraphed Zhang Zhijiang, the Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner, requesting that he quickly dispatch troops to intercept them. Jiang Kanru, deputy commander of the 2nd Cavalry Division, accompanied by staff member Mo Jinlong, took a car to Chuzhou this afternoon at 3 p.m., carrying funds to reward the officers and soldiers who suppressed the bandits in order to encourage them. (March 26th)

Local Dispatches

Songjiang

Summary of the Four-County Clearing Conference: After Cao Pang, commander of the Second Regiment of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Force, was ordered to concurrently serve as the temporary commander of the joint suppression efforts in Songjiang, Jinshan, Jiashan, and Pinghu counties, he actively suppressed bandits and captured key bandits such as Zhu Luo'e and others, who have been escorted to Songjiang for detention. Yesterday (26th), Commander Cao convened a four-county clearing conference. Those present included Jin Qingzhang, magistrate of Songjiang County; Qu Yunshu, secretary of Jinshan County; Ye Zheng'gang, representative of Jiashan County; Gao Xiaolan, representative of Pinghu County; Sun Kaixun, battalion commander of the Second Battalion of the Fourth Regiment of the Jiangsu Security Force; Bai Jizhi, battalion commander of the Second Battalion of the Second Regiment; Zhao Xunshi, battalion commander of the Second Battalion of the Seventh Regiment of the Zhejiang Security Force; Kai Jun, chief of the Zhejiang Xincang Security Group; Xue Zhichao, representative of the Second District of the Zhejiang Water Police; Xu Pucheng, chief of the First District of the Jiangsu Water Police; and local representatives, etc. The meeting was held at the headquarters. Commander Cao presided over the meeting, performed the ceremony, reported on the progress of bandit suppression, and then discussed the issues. The resolutions included: (1) Establishing security groups in each district; (2) Burying exposed corpses and coffins to prevent bandits from hiding weapons; (3) Continuing to blockade small rivers and ports during the clearing period. The above were proposed by Commander Cao. (1) To hold joint guarantee agreements, a new household register must first be created. It was resolved that each county would task the district and township heads to handle this. (2) Requesting that the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments each send two warships to patrol the coastal waters along Songjiang, Jinshan, Jiashan, and Pinghu counties. (3) Passing the investigation of bandits and the hiding of weapons to be handled according to the investigation methods. The above were proposed by Jinshan County. (1) If bandit traces are discovered in a certain area, the nearby military units should cooperate with the local police to search. (2) During the clearing period, those who capture bandits with significant circumstances in each county should be handed over to the headquarters, and those with minor circumstances should be interrogated by the respective counties. (3) It was resolved to grant leniency to accomplices who surrender themselves in accordance with the self-surrender regulations issued by Jiangsu Province. The above were proposed by Pinghu County. (1) Conscientiously inspect guns and check boats, and implement joint guarantees in accordance with the methods listed in the clearing instructions to eliminate bandits. (2) Inspecting wharf areas was passed by the Water Police Chief Xu. The remaining cases were lengthy and are omitted.

Confession of the Secretary of the Major Bandit: Zhu Zhenxin, secretary of the major bandit Zhu Luo'e, has also been captured. According to his interrogation by Commander Cao, he is 20 years old, with the courtesy name Zhichen, from Pinghu. He was a teacher at a certain school in Shanghai and was recommended by Fang Jie to serve as Zhu Luo'e's secretary, handling paperwork and correspondence, and was also apprenticed to him. In Qianwei, Luxiang, Langxia, Zhangjing, Dianshan, Jinjiazhuang, Taozhuang, and Gaoxu, he fought with the water and land police, resulting in over two hundred deaths. After the failure, Taibao A'shu escaped by sea, and A'e fled ashore. He was captured in Tianningzhuang, seized a civilian boat, and opened fire again in Zhujiaxing, resulting in over ten deaths. A'shu then led troops with weapons to fight again, but was defeated and the gang dispersed. Currently, Tao A'da, also known as Longhu, and Shen A'lu, Lu Yaosheng, are hiding in Shanghai. Shen Shouyi and his wife Shen Aihua claim to live in a small house at No. 180 Ximen Road, Shanghai, and were mistakenly arrested. Shen used to work in the Jiashan County Party Headquarters. Please allow them to be released on bail.

Clearing News from Headquarters: After the clearing conference at the headquarters yesterday, Commander Cao and the county magistrate representatives discussed the issue of bounty rewards for bandits. The bounty amounts for each bandit have now been compiled. The county offers 2,000 yuan for Taibao A'shu, with varying amounts for others, totaling 12,000 yuan. It was decided that the four counties would be responsible for raising the funds. Jinshan would contribute 4,000 yuan, Songjiang and Pinghu would each contribute 3,000 yuan, and Jiashan would contribute 2,000 yuan. The funds would be deposited in a bank and managed by a committee composed of the four county magistrates and one local representative each, to be used as needed. Since there have been no large-scale disturbances in the bandit areas since the gangs dispersed, the second phase of clearing work should be implemented. Three clearing brigades should be formed, with local authorities as the main body and the military as the auxiliary force. It is reported that implementation will begin in April. Commander Cao has been summoned to Beijing by Chairman Jiang tonight by night train to provide consultation on the compilation of revolutionary war history and to thank him for his promotion to major general.

Suzhou

Appeal Judgement in Shanghai Abduction Case: Lin Yongfang, an investigator from the Shanghai Women's Relief Association, discovered several abductors, including Lin Liu'shi, Lin Yijiao, Ren Chengwu, and Huang Zhenqing, on the Fujian Maru steamer bound for Fuzhou on January 13th. The Shanghai Local Court sentenced each of the offenders to imprisonment. The offenders, dissatisfied, appealed to the High Court. Yesterday (28th), Justice Li of the Second Criminal Division sentenced Lin Liu'shi to one year and two months of imprisonment, and Lin Yijiao, Ren Chengwu, and Huang Zhenqing each to six months of imprisonment. Xie Yingzhou, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Justice, Arrives in Suzhou to Inspect Prisons: Xie Yingzhou, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Justice, arrived in Suzhou from Beijing on the afternoon of the 27th. At 5 p.m. that afternoon, he went to the Third Sub-division Monitoring the Administration of Prisons on Siqian Street. Yesterday morning (28th), he went to the High Court for inspection, accompanied by President Lin and Section Chief of the Statistics Section Shi Zechen, among others, to inspect the Reformatory at the former Copper Bureau. Today, he is scheduled to tour places such as Mudu.

Appeal by Detention Center Director for Embezzlement: Zhang Zubin, former director of the Qingjiangpu Higher First Branch Court Detention Center, embezzled over 4,000 yuan of public funds. The High Court designated the Wuxian Local Court to investigate and hear the case last year. In September of last year, he was sentenced to eight months of imprisonment with a three-year suspended sentence. The embezzled funds were to be returned by Zhang Shoucuo. Zhang, dissatisfied with the verdict, appealed to the High Court. The Second Criminal Division has held several hearings, but no final verdict has been reached. Yesterday afternoon (28th) at 2 p.m., Justice Li summoned him again for trial, with a sentencing date to be set.

Murder Case in Dadangli Cracked, Culprit Arrested: On the 29th night of the old lunar calendar, six or seven robbers went to the home of fisherman Xia Jinbao in Dadangli, outside Fengmen, to steal fish and murdered Xia. Yesterday (28th), the detective team arrested the main culprit, Gu Fenghe (also known as Gu Xiao Mazi), and a suspect, Gu A'da, in Huguan. They were brought to the city for interrogation.

Fengxian

Two Suspects in Military Uniforms Arrested: The county government received a report from the Qianjiaqiao Town Security Group in the Fifth District that, while patrolling the Niulang Temple the night before, they found two suspects wearing military uniforms and carrying electric lamps. They were arrested, and several forged seals of a certain bank and a symbol of the 11th Division of the National Revolutionary Army were found near them. In addition, there was a travel permit issued by the division stating that Tan Yuzhong, a staff member of the division, was transporting his family from Beijing to Shanghai to Jinshanwei, and was allowed to travel by train without paying a fare along the way, and requesting that military and police agencies check and release him, and that he should not carry prohibited items. The permit was signed by Director Hu Lie and stamped with his seal. County Magistrate Shen interrogated the two suspects, but their confessions were evasive and they did not reveal the truth. County Magistrate Shen, suspecting the circumstances, sent them to the detention center for temporary custody and telegraphed the division today to clarify the situation.

Wuxi

Debt Group Holds Another Meeting Regarding Deposit Disputes: The Ding Shuangsheng silk and satin store in Chengzhong Dashiqiao, Wuxi County, experienced a dispute due to its inability to meet depositor withdrawals, which remains unresolved. It is reported that the depositors held another meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce at 2 p.m. yesterday. Over two hundred male and female depositor representatives attended and resolved to establish a depositor creditor group's executive committee, and elected members for each department. They set the 28th for another joint meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce, with the committee members and Ding Shuangsheng's representatives negotiating the continued operation of the store. It was resolved that Ding Xingchu would be responsible for raising 20,000 yuan in cash as a circulating fund for employees, with 10,000 yuan to be paid by the third of next month, and another 10,000 yuan by the tenth, in order to maintain operations.

Paper Store Bankrupt, Manager Arrested: The Tongxinchang Paper Store on Beida Street suddenly went bankrupt at the end of the lunar year, with debts owed to stores and depositors totaling over 100,000 yuan. Shareholder Peng Jingchu hired lawyers Zhou Yuyong and Zhou Chengqin to publish a notice for liquidation, but it was only talk without any concrete measures. At around 9 p.m. the day before yesterday, Cai Yourong, manager of the Ruiyu Store, and other store managers, dragged the store's manager, Peng Zhongpei, to the local Public Security Fifth Sub-bureau, which transferred him to the General Bureau. Yesterday, Police Chief Xu of the Public Security Bureau transferred him to the County Court for processing. Chief Prosecutor Yin Erkai opened a hearing and ordered Peng Zhongpei to provide a surety of 60,000 yuan. However, since he could not find a surety at the time, he was taken into custody pending investigation.

Actively Electing Representatives to the Electoral Assembly: County Magistrate and Electoral Supervisor Pan Zhongjia received instructions from Provincial Supervisor Hu to promptly dispatch personnel to the province to collect ballot boxes and other items for distribution and use. Supervisor Pan, upon receiving the order, dispatched Section Chief Shen Zao of the First Section to the province the day before yesterday to collect them. It is reported that after arriving in the town, Section Chief Shen contacted the National Election Department of the Provincial Government and obtained nine large and small ballot boxes, 41,000 election ballots, and eleven various registers. He returned to Wuxi yesterday to report to Supervisor Pan.

Changzhou

Bandit Boat and Hostages Found Outside Dabeimen: Sun Xichang's family near Cuiqiao, Wujin County, was robbed on the 16th of this month, and his three-year-old son, Fa Yuan, was kidnapped, with a ransom of 40,000 yuan demanded. Qian Jiahuan was dispatched to contact the bandits but there were no results. Patrol Officer Zhu Sen of the First Precinct of the Tenth Branch of the Public Security Bureau, upon receiving the report, conducted investigations and learned that Sun Linchang was involved in the case. He managed to capture him and interrogated him severely. Linchang revealed the details of the incident and said that the hostage was hidden in a derelict boat north of the city. Patrol Officer Zhu led police officers and escorted Sun Linchang to the city on the 26th. He met with Patrol Officer Wang Minwei of the local Public Security Precinct on the 27th at dawn and found a large barge under the east city wall of the North Diaqiao. Patrol Officer Zhu personally entered the cabin and saw a child who was identified by his parents as their son, Fa Yuan. He was handed to his father. The bandits Lü Zhongwei, Li Yazhou, boatmen Xue San and Xue Bian, and boatman Hu Wen were arrested and sent to the Public Security Bureau, which transferred them to the County Government for interrogation on the 28th.

The reason was unknown. The authorities were asked to investigate and respond quickly. Jiangyin

Reasons for the Joint Resignation of District Chiefs: Jiangyin County is divided into fourteen districts, each with a district chief. The county government's autonomy expenses and surtax revenues have been insufficient, and the districts have been in arrears for three or four months. On the 25th, the district chiefs went to the city for a district government meeting and requested funds from the Assets Office, but were unsuccessful. The district chiefs of eleven districts, excluding Chen Erchang of the Second District, Cao Zongduo of the Sixth District, and Huang Baoquan of the Thirteenth District, jointly submitted a request to the county government for permission to resign, led by Zhu Shuyun, the chief of the First District. County Magistrate Li, after reading it, returned the original request and ordered the Finance Bureau to find ways to raise funds to address the funding issue.

Summary of the Meeting on Pacification Zoning in Su-Chang: The Su-Chang Pacification Zone Command held a pacification meeting today (28th), convened by Commander Zhu Mian, with the county magistrates and water and land police chiefs of the eight counties under its jurisdiction, including Wuxi and Wuxian. The meeting was held at the Zhongshan Hall of the First District Office at 9 a.m. on the 28th. Those present included Pan Zhongjia, County Magistrate of Wuxi; Mao Mujun, Chief of the Second District of the Water Public Security Team; Fang Qi, Captain of the Wujin Police Team; Qian Wenyu, Captain of the Changshu Police Team; Du Hongyi, Captain of the Wuxian Police Team; Shen Gaozhen, Chief of the Third District of the Water Public Security Team; Shi Mingcun, Section Chief of the Wujiang County Government; Qin Zhongying, Chief of the Kunshan Public Security Bureau; Xi Ziwei, Chief of the Taicang Public Security Bureau and Captain of the Police Team; Li Leng, County Magistrate of Jiangyin; and Shen Hualong, Captain of the 20th Brigade of the Water Public Security Team. Zhu Mian presided over the meeting and reported the reasons for convening the meeting. The representatives of the eight counties then reported on the defense situation in their respective counties. Discussions and resolutions were then initiated on various issues related to bandit suppression, clearing, and defense. After the meeting on various agendas, a group photo was taken and the meeting adjourned.

Wu Cheng, Investigating Judge, Goes to the Countryside to Examine the Murder Case: Fisherman Shi Xiaobao and others of Chen Sanwei'an, Wangjiadai, and Yu Xiaobao had a dispute over catching hairtail at the Wushan Port, resulting in a murder. Yesterday, Investigating Judge Wu, accompanied by Examiner Cao, went to the countryside to examine the corpse. The deceased Yu Xiaobao was confirmed to have been injured before his death. According to Yu Rubao, brother of the deceased, during fishing on the third day of the lunar month, Shi Xiaobao and others came to争夺the place. Shi A'bao (i.e., Lai Lang) grabbed and twisted me. Shi Xiaobao (Shi Xiaobao said yesterday that his brother Lai Lang killed him, completely shifting the blame) then hit my brother's head with an iron tip from the mast, resulting in his death. Yu Guiqing, father of the deceased, and Yu Zhou, wife of the deceased, also provided the same testimony. Investigating Judge Wu then ordered the deceased to be coffined and transported back. He ordered Yu Rubao to report the case on the 28th and then returned to the city.

The Seventh District Sub-Branch has filed an accusation with the higher-level Party Headquarters, which has been forwarded to the County Government, requesting investigation and handling.

Yangzhou

Fire at Xiaohongqiao Kills Two Children: At 5 a.m. on the 26th, a fire broke out at the Wang Ziba pot-making shop in Xianzhen Xiaohongqiao due to Wang Zi getting up to urinate and carelessly starting a fire. Two children, one eight years old and one a few weeks old, were burned to death. The fire also spread to several workshops of the Ma family next door.

Zhenjiang

Chamber of Commerce Calls Another Meeting of County Chambers of Commerce: The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce previously convened a meeting of representatives from various county chambers of commerce in Zhenjiang due to the provincial government's business tax regulations violating the departmental outline, and resolved to petition in Beijing. The Ministry of Finance has now approved the reduction of business tax rates in Jiangsu Province. The previous unit-based taxation has been changed to industry-based taxation. The previous tax rules, with a maximum levy of 20 per mille, have been reduced to 10 per mille. However, the provincial government intends to have the collection of this tax handled by the county chambers of commerce, which is of great importance. It cannot be approved without convening a joint discussion of the county chambers of commerce. Therefore, a circular has been issued setting a date of April 1st to invite representatives of the county chambers of commerce to come to Zhenjiang for a meeting to discuss whether to accept it.

A List of Pacification Commanders and Their Station Locations: The Jiangsu Provincial Security Office previously reported to the Pacification Commissioner's Office that Qingpu was assigned to the Songhu District and Taicang was assigned to the Suchang District. It is reported that the locations and areas of jurisdiction of the commanders in each district have been decided. The Xu-Hai Zone has its base in Zhangyao Wan with jurisdiction over twelve counties; the Huai-Yang Zone has its base in Qingjiang with jurisdiction over fourteen counties; the Tong-Hai Zone has its base in Yangzhou with jurisdiction over eight counties; the Su-Chang Zone has its base in Jiangyin with jurisdiction over eight counties; and the Song-Hu Zone has its base in Songjiang with jurisdiction over nine counties.

New Staff of the Financial Department's Saline Land Office: Chen Qicai, Director of the Jiangsu Financial Department, has been actively preparing to establish a Saline Land Office. Prisoner Escapes from Yuyao Prison: Yuyao County Prison holds a large number of prisoners for theft cases. Prison officials and guards have always been very strict in guarding them. Unexpectedly, at 7 p.m. last night (26th), the prisoners in the prison colluded and escaped. They first secretly transported weapons inside. At about 7 p.m., the prisoners held weapons, broke down the doors and windows, poured out, and fled in all directions. Only one prisoner, Shi Guangtong, was apprehended by police officer Wang Xuan of the Second Precinct. The remaining twelve prisoners, including Wang Xinda, escaped.

Fire at Yaoxing Street Last Night: A fire broke out on the third floor of the Zhichang Ginseng Store on Yaoxing Street at over 6 p.m. in this port last night. Fortunately, the Lin'an Guild's fire brigade and various volunteer fire brigades arrived at the scene and quickly extinguished the fire, preventing it from spreading. After investigation, only the second-floor building of the Yichang Store and the gatehouse of the Zikang Money Shop and the sun deck of the Shihexia Clock Store were burned, with an estimated loss of 500 yuan.

Hefei

Provincial Government Dispatches Personnel to Supervise Opium Poppy Eradication: Although the opium scourge in Hefei has been strictly prohibited by government officials, it has not been eradicated. This spring, opium seedlings in the four rural townships are still dazzling, especially in the three, four, and five districts in the northeast. Local officials and the Opium Poppy Eradication Promotion Association have sent personnel to the countryside to persuade people to voluntarily eradicate them. The area near the city has been somewhat effective, but the distant villages are still indifferent. The provincial government has dispatched inspector He Nanseng to Hefei to督率and promote the eradication. On the afternoon of the 22nd, a meeting was held at the County Government with the heads of the twenty districts to decide to instruct the heads of each district to eradicate the opium seedlings by April 20th and provide a written guarantee. In the future, if opium seedlings are found in a certain district, the head of that district will be severely punished.

Eight Nations Compete for the International Football Cup

China Wins the Championship for the Second Time

Yesterday, a Score of One to Zero, Overpowering England

No Victory or Defeat for Either Side in Ninety Minutes

Chen Zhenhe Scores the Winning Goal in Extra Time

Heaven blesses China, after hardship, difficulty, upheaval, and displacement, they finally scored in the last five minutes of extra time. General Blackface Chen Zhenhe's divine foot launched, the ball broke through the net with a thunderous sound. The flag of the Blue Sky with a White Sun was raised high above the flags of other countries. The wind seemed to announce to people that these are the brave men under our revolutionary banner, who have displayed their spirit of indomitable courage and defeated the strong and invincible England, thus gaining the honor of holding the leadership in maritime football and retaining the International Football Championship for another year. All of our people should congratulate together.

(1) Eight Nations Compete, China Takes the Lead

This year's participants include China, England, Scotland, Jewish, Portugal, France, Japan, and Germany, a total of eight teams. Except for France, Japan, and Germany, whose strength is relatively weak, the rest are all strong teams with equal strength. The Jewish team surprisingly defeated Scotland with a score of three to two, and then tied England with a score of to two in extra time. In the replay, the Jewish team lost to England with a score of two to six. They first defeated Japan with a score of twenty-three to zero, and then defeated the Jewish team to win the final. Germany forfeited to Portugal. China first defeated Germany with a score of four to zero, and then defeated Portugal with a score of three to zero. Finally, the Chinese and English teams competed in the final yesterday afternoon at 3:00, with China winning the championship with a score of one to zero.

Forfeiture

(2) Revolutionary Heroes Glorify History

Our country's participation in this competition began in 1923, which is eight years ago. The first competition's results were mediocre, but this showed our determination for international competition. Since then, we have worked hard to train, and in the second year (i.e., 1924-25), we were able to meet England in the final. At that time, the magnificent and enthusiastic cheers of more than ten thousand spectators in the China baseball field still echo in our minds. However, China lost to England with a score of zero to four. Later, in 1927-28, China and England met again in the final. At that time, China's strength was quite strong and had the hope of winning the championship. Unexpectedly, the Jinan University football team had players traveling in Southeast Asia, such as Feng Yunyou, Chen Zhenhe, and Liang Guansong, who did not join, which affected the team's strength and led to a tragic defeat of two to four. Last year (1929-30), the Chinese team won the final for the third time. China defeated Scotland with a score of two to zero and won the championship. Years of hard work were finally realized. This year, yesterday, China once again played against England in the final. As a result, China won with a score of one to zero and continued to hold the championship. The Shanghai International Football Championship competition began in 1908. Except for the four years of suspension during the European War, it has been held every year without interruption. England has won the most times, followed by Scotland. The past championships are listed below:

1908｜09 England 1909｜10 England

1910｜11 England 1911｜12 Ireland

1912｜13 England 1913｜14 England

1914｜15 England 1915｜19 Suspended

1919｜20 England 1920｜21 England

1921｜22 England 1922｜23 England

1923｜24 England 1924｜25 Scotland

1925｜26 Scotland 1926｜27 Scotland

1927｜28 England 1928｜29 Portugal

1929｜30 China 1930｜31 China

Looking at the above table, there have been a total of 19 competitions. England has won 18 times, Scotland 3 times, Ireland once, Portugal once, and China won the championship for the first time last year. This year, China defeated the stubborn England with a score of one to zero, and also has the glory of winning the championship for two consecutive years.

(3) Over Ten Thousand Fans Sing Triumphantly Together

The news that China and England would meet in the Shen Garden spread far and wide, and a large number of spectators gathered. On that day, the sun shone brightly and the spring breeze was warm. As soon as the bell rang, people from all walks of life flocked to the stadium. The tram and bus business was booming. Every car that arrived was like a tide rushing down and running to the stadium to be the first to arrive. Before 2:00, the stadium was filled with tens of thousands of people, extremely crowded. The cars parked outside the stadium were also densely packed, almost covering the entire area. It is estimated that there were over 15,000 people, setting a record for this year. The fierce battle of ninety minutes was fought with victory and defeat extended to overtime. China finally won the championship with a score of one to zero. The sounds of firecrackers and cheers echoed each other, shaking the surrounding fields. At that time, the sun was setting and the bloody battle came to an end. Mr. Hamson, the honorary secretary of the Westerners' Association, personally presented the International Cup to Dai Linjing, the captain of the Chinese team, and shook hands to congratulate him. The two teams shouted "Long live!" to each other and retreated in a courteous manner. The crowd admired the heroes with utmost sincerity, surrounding the brave men like stars surrounding the moon. They carried the captain and sang and walked. Dai苦's number of requests for directions only stopped then. Such a lively scene is rarely seen in previous football history.

Chongming Schools' Teachers and Staff Resume Work

County Magistrate is Responsible for Raising Funds

Due to the excessive amount of fees owed by the Education Bureau to various schools in Chongming, a unanimous work slowdown occurred. The Education Bureau telegraphed the county government to allocate funds for repayment and督促instructed all schools to resume classes as usual. After receiving the telegram, the county government attached great importance to it and decided at the county administrative meeting on the 21st to first issue one month's expenses to each school within one week, issue two months' expenses within two weeks, and other proposals to guarantee education fees. On the 26th, the representatives of the teachers and staff who went to the province returned to Chongming and stated that they should agree to resume classes first. Xu Shang's method, the county government also agreed to issue one and a half months' expenses before the resumption of classes and another half month's expenses within one week, with County Magistrate Shen responsible. On the evening of the 26th, the work slowdown committee decided to reluctantly accept this method and notified all schools to resume work together from the 27th, and decided to convene representatives from all schools on the 29th to discuss the fundamental solution for clearing education fees in detail in order to achieve a satisfactory result. However, Deputy Director Zhang Peishu has not yet returned due to his inability to cope.

They were immediately sworn into office.

All Sectors of the City Hold Meetings to Commemorate

At 9:00 AM in the City Party Headquarters

Today (29th) is the anniversary of the revolutionary martyrs who died at Yellow Flower Mound. The Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters has already notified all agencies, organizations, and party headquarters at all levels to send four representatives to the City Party Headquarters to hold a commemorative meeting. Rural areas and various agencies, organizations, and schools farther away from the city may also hold separate commemorative ceremonies. All sectors of the city will fly flags at half-mast and close business for one day, and suspend entertainment to express their condolences.

Today is the anniversary of the martyrdom of the 72 Martyrs of Yellow Flower Mound. All agencies will take a day off to express their condolences. The French Concession Water and Electricity workers plan to request the company authorities to provide an additional day off since today falls on a Sunday. Lu Guanhong and Zhang Renjun were specially appointed as representatives to first negotiate with the Chinese compradore Shen Shumei, and then Shen accompanied Lu and Zhang, two representatives to ask the foreman. Jianghai Customs Requests Foreign Warships to Withdraw from the Huangpu River

And Confiscate Naval Buoys Set Up in the Port. Jianghai Customs has recently received an order from the National Government to write to the consuls general of various countries in Shanghai, requesting warships from various countries not to dock in the Huangpu River, and requesting the confiscation of naval buoys set up by Britain, the United States, France, Japan, and Italy in the port of Shanghai. The Jianghai Customs' reason is that the existence of such buoys is enough to cause fear among travelers and Shanghai pilots from various countries, and the initial port development plan did not anticipate the entry and exit of such huge ships as today. According to customs officials, if this continues, accidents will inevitably occur near the naval buoys in the future for huge ships traveling in the river. After receiving this letter, the consuls of various countries said that this request was not only reasonable but also inevitable, but the result is currently unpredictable.

Another Jiang'an Ship Incident Involving Gambling Bandits' Extortion and Assault

Please Request Headquarters to Send Troops to Protect

Otherwise Passengers Will Take Foreign Ships

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiangshun ship was previously killed by gambling bandits. The report was纪recorded by this newspaper. Now one thing has not been completed and another thing has happened. A disaster of disturbance and extortion by gambling bandits occurred in the Jiang'an ship of the Yangtze River Shipping Bureau. The situation heard is recorded in detail as follows:

Initiating a Quarrel by Asking for Food The previous Jiangshun ship gambling bandits initiated a quarrel by asking for food in Huangshi Port. The same is true for the Jiang'an incident this time. It was found that when the Jiang'an ship left Shanghai on the 25th and sailed upstream, the accounting office began to sell tickets. Suddenly, more than 30 gambling bandits in the ship, all wearing uniforms, rushed to the door of the accounting office and demanded lunch from the crew. The crew members, punished by the murder of the cook of the Jiangshun ship, comforted the bandits with kind words, saying that they would send the food as soon as it was cooked. The bandits refused and insisted on getting the food immediately. At that time, there were more than 100 armed comrades in the ship. The bandits used words to instigate them to cause trouble with the accounting office and others, and they were about to use force. Finally, one crew member was twisted and beaten by the bandits. Fortunately, the entire crew rose up to rescue him and save his life, but the bandits continued to cause trouble.

Accusing a Passenger of Drowning When the ship arrived in Jiangyin, another 30 to 40 accomplices of the bandits, all like retired soldiers, joined the bandit group and made things difficult for the crew. They claimed that a passenger had been pushed into the river by your crew and had drowned. This passenger had boarded the ship at the same time as them. The life was at stake and they demanded the crew to pay a huge sum for compensation. The situation was very tense. Operations Director Liu Jida and others stepped forward to resolve the matter and proved that no passenger had been pushed into the water and died. The bandits relied on their power to forcibly make unreasonable demands. The passengers on the entire ship were panicked and rose up to prove that this had not happened. The bandits had no excuse and planned another revenge.

Detaining the Ship for Negotiation When the ship arrived in Zhenjiang, some bandits reported to the Public Security Bureau that a homicide had occurred on the Jiang'an ship. Upon receiving the report, the Public Security Bureau urgently sent a large number of constables to the ship to investigate the case thoroughly. They immediately detained the Jiang'an ship and wanted to arrest the crew members to go to the bureau for questioning. The Operations Director came forward to state that no passenger had fallen into the water and that the incident was a false accusation by gambling bandits for extortion. After various negotiations and investigations, it was confirmed that there were no conclusive facts before the ship was released.

Requesting Military Protection Since the capital garrison headquarters transferred the garrison troops to Suzhou for training, dozens or hundreds of gambling bandits have often traveled up and down the Yangtze River ships, deceiving and extorting in every possible way, and often resorting to violence. Passengers regard Chinese merchant ships as a dangerous place and dare not take them. Recently, the passengers on British and Japanese river ships have been very crowded. The Chinese ships' business is declining. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company reported the Jiang'an ship's accident in detail to the headquarters, requesting that special service soldiers be sent to the ship for protection as soon as possible, otherwise it will be difficult to navigate.

The Social Affairs Bureau Orders Rong Zongjing to Postpone the Takeover of the Sanxin Cotton Mill

Employees of the Sanxin Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road, which announced its sale, have demanded that post-employment arrangements be made first and have refused to hand over the mill. This has been unresolved for many days. Yesterday was the second time the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau convened the parties involved to attempt mediation. The old and new mill owners still did not attend. The labor representatives requested that the handover be postponed until the matter is resolved. The bureau agreed to their request and rescheduled the meeting for April 1st. The details obtained are recorded as follows:

Convening Mediation - The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was ordered to handle the sale case of the Sanxin Cotton Mill. It was heard that on the 26th, the parties involved were convened for questioning, but the old and new mill owners did not attend. A public notice was issued, and the meeting was rescheduled for 1:00 PM on the 28th to question all parties involved in the case, including the Cotton Textile Industry Association of the Third Special District, the new buyer Rong Zongjing, and the Sanxin mill owner Sheng Ze Cheng, and to attempt mediation. Tian Sanzi and others from the Cotton Textile Industry Association of the Third Special District attended on time, but the old and new mill owners, Rong Zongjing and Sheng Ze Cheng, still did not attend. The case officer Xu Zhi instructed the labor representatives to return and await further processing.

Labor Representatives' Submission - The Cotton Textile Industry Association of the Third Special District submitted a document to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating: "Regarding the report that the new buyer of the Sanxin Cotton Mill is using hooligans to undermine our labor union, we request your review. Since the sale of the Sanxin Mill, the old and new owners have not completed the handover, and our request to the mill owner for severance pay has not been resolved. The new owner has even bought off unscrupulous elements to incite workers to spread rumors in order to shake the will of our entire membership. The association members witnessed this and were extremely alarmed. In the event of unexpected events arising from this labor-management dispute, this association will not be responsible. Before the old mill owner resolves the post-employment issues for the workers, we beg your bureau to instruct the new mill owner to temporarily postpone the takeover and urgently stop all destructive acts. This is our earnest prayer."

Order to Rong Zongjing - Yesterday, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to Rong Zongjing, the general manager of Shenxin Textile Company, the buyer of the machinery and factory buildings of the Sanxin Cotton Mill, stating: "Regarding the matter of complying with the order, in the case of your company purchasing the Sanxin Cotton Mill, you previously stated that you were willing to assist in resolving the labor dispute, so you were permitted to take over first. However, this bureau convened mediation, and the old and new mill owners repeatedly failed to attend, resulting in the case remaining unresolved. You are hereby ordered to comply with the order to postpone the takeover until the severance pay dispute for the mill's employees is resolved, to avoid inciting unexpected events."

Instructions to the Labor Union - Yesterday, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received a submission from the Cotton Textile Industry Association of the Third Special District stating that the new buyer of the Sanxin Mill was using hooligans to undermine the union and requesting instructions to temporarily postpone the takeover. The bureau issued instructions to the labor union, stating: "The submission has been noted and approved to order a temporary postponement of the takeover. You are to be notified and await a resolution."

Notification to the Mill Owner - Yesterday, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau published a notice in the newspaper for Sheng Ze Cheng, the mill owner of the Sanxin Cotton Mill, and Sheng Yujun, the manager, stating: "Regarding the announcement, in this sale of the mill, you neither submitted a request beforehand nor dispatched representatives to attend the mediation convened by this bureau afterward, which is highly inappropriate. In addition to instructing Rong Zongjing, the buyer of the mill, to temporarily postpone the takeover, a meeting for mediation is scheduled for 1:00 PM on April 1st. Sheng Ze Cheng and Sheng Yujun, or a responsible representative appointed by them, are ordered to attend the bureau on time to listen to the mediation and not to violate this order again, to avoid inciting unexpected events. This is specifically announced."

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's Advice to the Municipal Council

Opposing the Assessment of Police Rates Based on Estimated Rent

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement yesterday, stating: "Regarding the fact that our Chamber has recently received reports from various businesses stating that the police rates collected by your Council will be calculated based on estimated rent and implemented from January 1st of this year, requesting negotiations. Our Chamber believes that the purpose of this change in collection method by your Council is solely to expand your Council's financial income without regard to the sharp increase in the burden on citizens. This method is unfair and will also provide landlords with an excuse to increase rents. Therefore, this action by your Council will have two impacts: (1) It is tantamount to an invisible increase in the tax rate; (2) It is tantamount to inducing landlords to raise rents. At a time when the global market is depressed and this city is no exception, your Council's sudden action will increase the burden on citizens in two ways, which will inevitably arouse resentment among the majority of citizens in the Settlement towards your Council. This year, your Council has been striving to foster harmonious relations with the Chinese within the Settlement. If this action is implemented, it will be tantamount to abandoning years of effort in one fell swoop, which is regrettable. Therefore, our Chamber sincerely offers its advice and requests that this proposal be canceled and that police rates continue to be collected based on actual rent. This would be greatly appreciated."

Shareholders' Meeting of the Shanghai Waterworks Company of the International Settlement

Water Prices May Increase Significantly This Year After Revision

The Shanghai Waterworks Company of the International Settlement held a shareholders' meeting at the company yesterday, reported the "North China Daily News." Chairman Liddell reported on the company's business performance last year, stating that the revenue from user accounts in the Settlement was taels 3,832,281.46, an increase of more than 390,000 taels compared to taels 2,434,725.93 in the previous year. However, expenses also increased from taels 1,077,365.34 to taels 1,320,984.19, an increase of approximately 240,000 taels. The net profit was taels 1,511,297.27, an increase of more than 150,000 taels compared to taels 1,357,360.69 in the previous year. The increase in expenses last year was primarily due to the sharp decline in silver prices and frequent fluctuations in exchange rates, and secondly, the amount of water supplied also increased. A total of 14,320 million gallons of water were supplied last year, compared to only 13,148 million gallons in the previous year. The increase in revenue was largely due to the surcharge approved by the Municipal Council. The net profit from user accounts in the Settlement last year was taels 1,065,002.16, an increase of more than 139,000 taels compared to taels 925,461.36 in the previous year. However, after paying the interim dividend of 3.125% in the fall, with an exchange rate of 1 shilling 6 pence, taels 484,677.09 was spent. The remaining net profit must be added to the dividend reserve fund to raise taels 960,209.90 to pay the final dividend for Class A shares at 5.85%, Class B shares at 3.875%, and Class C shares at 4.875%, with an exchange rate of 1 shilling 3 pence 875. The net profit from user accounts outside the Settlement and from ship users was taels 88,876.44 last year, compared to taels 121,605.64 in the previous year. Revenue also decreased from taels 346,538.79 to taels 331,713.06. Although the water consumption by ships increased significantly due to the water shortage in Hong Kong, the water consumption outside the Settlement decreased sharply due to the expiration of the water borrowing agreement with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Plant, resulting in a decrease in revenue compared to previous years. It is proposed to distribute dividends this time at 2 shillings 8 pence for Class A shares and 1 shilling 6 pence for Class B shares. In terms of engineering, two large pumping machines, each with a capacity of 600,000 gallons per hour, were installed last year, as well as two large water inlet machines and a batch of rapid filters. A 40-inch main water pipe is currently being laid from the Yangshupu Pumping Station to the Jiangxi Road Water Tower, with a value of nearly £50,000. He then described the negotiations with the Chinese Association on the increased water surcharge and the payment of taxes in the fall and stated that the revised water prices this year, in accordance with the contract signed with the Municipal Council in 1928, may increase significantly compared to the old prices. This surcharge is only a precursor to the price increase, but the company's water prices, even including the surcharge, are not excessive and are lower than those in many cities and towns in England. The company has long advocated abolishing the system of charging based on rent and switching to a water meter system. Fortunately, the Municipal Council has expressed its agreement, so...

Page 14

The revised water prices submitted to the Municipal Council this year will be based on the water meter system. However, there are still many related issues that need to be resolved before implementation, so it cannot be realized in a short period of time. However, the company firmly believes that it is necessary to switch to a water meter system for the benefit of all users. Regarding the issue of supplying water to the area west of the Public Concession, the company is in negotiations with the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau and the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. After the chairman's report, the various proposals were passed and new directors were elected, and the meeting was adjourned.

Customs Procedures for Restricted Goods Transportation

National Government Passport Required for Release

Deputy Commissioner of Customs of the Jianghai Customs, Kreder, issued a public notice yesterday regarding the procedures for transporting prohibited goods, stating: "Regarding the announcement, in accordance with the 'Regulations on Transportation Passports for Nitrate and Mineral Products' formulated by the National Government, the following items should be included in the list of customs prohibited and restricted transportation items: potassium nitrate, air nitrate, potassium chloride, potassium perchlorate, hydrochloric acid, red phosphorus, white phosphorus, yellow phosphorus, and other items. Merchants transporting the above items should immediately submit the National Government passport and Ministry of Finance's Foreign Affairs Transportation Document to the Customs for inspection in accordance with the 'Measures for Restricting the Transportation of Materials for Manufacturing Explosive Items' before they can be released."

For those who do not have relatives and friends in Shanghai, the office of the organizing committee will hand them over to the post office for registered mail to complete the procedures. It is heard that most of the returned items have been distributed, and the office of the organizing committee will be closed soon.
