Steps to Excavate the Shentan Shoal

Starting with Surveying

The Dredging Bureau, based on the suggestions of shipping merchants and transportation merchants, requested that the Shentan Shoal (i.e., Hidden Sand) at the mouth of the Yangtze River be excavated to allow large ships from all countries to enter and exit without the need for time-consuming detours. The Bureau convened a meeting and decided to dredge the shoal. The Inspector General of Customs proposed that the cost of excavating the Shentan Shoal be covered by adding a dredging surcharge to import duties, and that 3% of the value be levied according to the new tariff, which was submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implemented from April 1st. It has been reported in the newspapers. It is now learned that the Bureau's Chief Engineer, Chatley, is preparing for the excavation of the Shentan Shoal. As this is a major undertaking, it is necessary to conduct a detailed and final survey to determine whether the Hidden Sand is sedimentary and to prepare accordingly. It is heard that he has ordered the surveying section, led by Deputy Engineer Xia Ruifu, to go to the mouth of the Yangtze River to conduct a final and thorough survey.

Various Industries Requesting Reduction of Business Tax

Insurance Industry - Recently, the Ministry of Finance revised the "Regulations on Business Tax in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai," stipulating that the insurance industry will be taxed at a rate of 20 per thousand, which will soon be submitted to the Central Political Conference and the ministries and departments for review and promulgation. The Shanghai Insurance Industry Association convened a temporary emergency meeting yesterday at 2:30 PM, attended by more than 30 members, to discuss ways to request the central government to reduce or exempt business tax. Liu Shisun was elected as chairman and Hu Xiansi was elected as secretary. After the meeting, the members all agreed that the insurance industry is an undertaking that develops the national economy, and that the Chinese insurance industry has been repeatedly oppressed by foreign merchants, and its business is declining. It is now in its infancy and requires government protection and promotion to achieve development. However, it is now burdened with this tax, which it cannot afford. It was decided to appoint representatives to prepare documents to petition the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Ministry of Finance, and other ministries and departments. Li Shuxiong, Lu Yuequan, Liu Shisun, Guo Baming, Hu Yongqi, and Pan Xuean were elected as representatives to go to Beijing to petition. The representatives are currently preparing everything and will leave for Beijing in a few days.

Paint Industry - The Paint Industry Association believes that the implementation of business tax in this city has a significant impact on the burden on the various guilds in the paint industry. A general meeting of members was convened the day before yesterday at 3:00 PM. More than 40 letters from members of the carpentry guild were received on that afternoon, stating that the business tax stipulated in Jiangsu Province for paints and varnishes is 2 per thousand, while Western-style furniture and rosewood and sandalwood industries are still taxed at 10 per thousand. If this is passed and implemented, they will not be able to afford it, and their industries are on the verge of bankruptcy. In addition to requesting a reduction, there is no need to attend the meeting, etc. Therefore, a temporary executive committee meeting was held instead. Du Gengsheng was elected as chairman, and Min Xingchu was elected as secretary. Zhang Fukang, Zhou Shanqing, Ling Youqiao, and Chen Yougeng, and others jointly deliberated that the business tax stipulated in Jiangsu Province for rosewood and sandalwood industries was initially 20 per thousand. After the association sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, it was approved for revision, and a 10 per thousand tax was proposed. However, from the import of raw materials to the production of furniture, rosewood and sandalwood go through four tax payment procedures. If business tax is levied again, it will be difficult to maintain a livelihood. Therefore, they requested that the gentlemen discuss this at length. It was decided to elect Du Gengsheng, Zhang Fukang, Ling Youqiao, and Zhou Shanqing as representatives to petition the relevant authorities and seek solutions. Next, Ma Yunxiang, Xu Guoqing, Wang Shengcai, Ma Zhigang, and others deliberated on revising the regulations of the various guilds. It was decided to schedule a meeting of members of the six guilds to discuss the matter. The meeting adjourned. The secretary drafted a memorial that evening, and the four representatives, Du Zhang Ling Zhou, went to the Shanghai South Municipal Government to petition yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. They were received by Mr. Chen Xilu, who, after hearing the representatives' statements, believed that the business tax on paints, varnishes, Western-style furniture, and rosewood and sandalwood had special characteristics and that it was necessary to request the government to consider the hardships of the merchants and transfer the petition to the various ministries and departments of the National Government for consideration of reduction or exemption to maintain their livelihoods. Mr. Chen accepted the petition and promised to report it to the mayor. The representatives felt satisfied with the purpose of the petition and took their leave. They then went to the Bureau of Finance, where they were received by Mr. Fang Zhongyan of the Bureau, and the result was also very satisfactory.

Cotton Weaving and Manufacturing Industry Should Be Exempt from Business Tax

Conversation with a Leader in the Cotton Weaving Industry

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Mr. Zhu Qi, a leader in the cotton weaving industry, to ask for his opinion on the issue of whether the cotton weaving and manufacturing industry should pay business tax. According to him, Article 4 of the "Detailed Rules for the Collection of Unified Tax on Cotton Yarn" promulgated by the Ministry of Finance states that cotton yarn that has already paid the unified tax and the cotton cloth directly woven from this type of cotton yarn may be exempt from any other types of national, provincial, or local taxes in the interior. This means that all products manufactured by yarn factories and cotton weaving factories are exempt from any other types of national, provincial, or local taxes other than the unified tax. Furthermore, the term "any type" includes goods tax, business tax, and other types of taxes in the national, provincial, or local categories. According to Article 1 of the "Measures for Collecting Business Tax" in various provinces, those who have already paid special steady donations levied by the central government are exempt from paying business tax. It is heard that yarn factories are exempt from paying business tax based on the former regulations. The position of the various factories in the cotton weaving and manufacturing industry is the same as that of yarn factories and should be exempted from business tax. The unified tax paid on cotton yarn, a product of yarn factories, is actually borne by the cotton weaving and manufacturing industry. Yarn factories are only acting as collectors of taxes and enjoy the right to be exempt from paying business tax. Cotton weaving factories are the actual payers of the unified tax. If they cannot be exempted from paying business tax, it would not be fair in terms of reason and logic.

Silk Factories in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai Held a Meeting Yesterday

Silk factories in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai held a meeting of the Special Relief Committee yesterday (the 28th) at 4:00 PM regarding the silk industry public debt. The attendees included Shen Huachen, Zhu Jing'an, Chu Huiseng, Qian Fenghao, Xue Shou, (Chen Pinsan's representative), Yang Yuchu, Zhang Zizhen, Cheng Bingruo, (Shan Youxian's representative), Zhang Yunsheng, Huang Jinjin, Wang Xiaolai, Huang Jinfan, (Zhang Yunsheng's representative), and more than a dozen others. The meeting was chaired by Shen Huachen and began with a ritual, followed by Chairman Shen's report on the purpose of the meeting and the reading of the original text of the telegram from the Ministry urging the issuance of public debt. The discussion then began on how to proceed. The members believed that the silkworm season in Zhejiang Province was the earliest. Farmers in Hangzhou and Shaoxing were preparing for silkworm farming. Qingming is the time for hatching seeds, and Guyu is the time for collecting ants, which is the usual practice for silkworm farming. However, farmers, considering the sluggish silk market last year and the failure of silk factories, were on the verge of bankruptcy. The silk merchants were asked whether they would collect cocoons as usual, and inquiries were made to the cocoon dealers in the various regions. In the past, silk merchants would contract with cocoon dealers during the winter to secure cocoon purchases for the following year. This year, during the Qingming Festival, no one had contracted to rent the cocoon dealerships in the various regions. The cocoon dealers were gathering in Shanghai to contact their counterparts to negotiate the rental of cocoon dealerships. The members believed that the sharp drop in silk prices last year had severely impacted their businesses, resulting in a loss of capital. The financial sector was unable to repay the advance payment for silkworm cocoons. This year, factories borrowing cocoons to start production are facing the difficulty of selling their products due to the current sluggish silk market and high prices. There is no definite date for the government's issuance of relief public debt. Silver and money lenders believe that the silk factory industry is still in arrears and will be unable to provide loans for cocoon purchases this year. Therefore, they are not sure whether they will be able to collect cocoons this year. They hope that the public debt will be issued as soon as possible so that the livelihoods of farmers, social finance, and foreign trade can be maintained. It was decided to send another telegram to the Ministry to urge them to issue the public debt. The meeting adjourned.

Tea Industry Commission Increases

Has Requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Notify the Bureau of Social Affairs for Record

Tea merchants and brokerage houses have always charged a commission of 4% for buying and selling tea on behalf of customers (i.e., deducting 4 yuan for every 100 yuan). This regulation is still the old rule from 30 years ago. With the increasing cost of living, many tea merchants and brokerage houses have been unable to maintain their businesses and have closed down. It is heard that the industry has decided to increase the commission by 2% in order to compensate, following the example of Zhejiang Province. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has been requested to notify the Bureau of Social Affairs for record.

Changjiang Ship Crew Members Released from Songshan Road Police Station Yesterday

Annamese Returned to Take Defence

The Remaining Negotiations Were Conducted In Shanghai

The crew members of the Changjiang, who were in distress, had been residing at the Songshan Road French Police Station for several days. Yesterday morning at around 8:00 AM, personnel from the French Consulate went to instruct the crew members to pack their luggage and transport it in a large car to the French Consulate near the Bund on Gongguan Road to await processing. The crew members complied with the instructions and boarded the car. However, the car drove directly to the China Merchants Wharf in Nanshi. The French mail ship, the "A Tad De Na," approached and forced them to board the ship. The Austrian crew members were in uproar and unanimously refused to board. Later, Li Zuyao, a representative of the Seamen's Union, arrived and negotiated. As a result, the Guangdong and Zhejiang crew members were allowed to stay in Shanghai. An Appeal for Disaster Prevention in Haizhou

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association received a letter yesterday from Reverend Ming, a Western missionary of the Haizhou Presbyterian Church. The gist of the translation is that the area has always been known for its fertile land, but in recent years, the western and eastern districts have suffered from floods. Every harvest season, vast tracts of fertile land are submerged, causing repeated disasters and extreme hardship for the people. The root cause of the deep suffering is that the waterways are blocked, resulting in annual losses of life and property. For the fundamental purpose of disaster prevention, it is proposed to dredge the waterways and open new canals to allow accumulated water to flow from Haizhou, branch off to Shuyang, and enter the sea to discharge water and prevent future disasters. Three million yuan has already been raised, but one to two million yuan is still needed. They would like to request assistance from the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association. It is reported that all of the association's relief funds have been remitted to relieve the urgent needs in Shaanxi and are completely exhausted. They feel helpless in the face of this important disaster prevention plan. It is commendable that the missionary, as a foreigner, is doing his utmost to benefit the Chinese people and provide fundamental relief. It is hoped that benevolent individuals will provide assistance to complete this charitable endeavor.

Local News Two

Constable Nie Dianrong

Commendable Demise in the Line of Duty

Police Department Grants Compensation of One Thousand Yuan

Funeral Scheduled for Tomorrow

Chinese and Western Detectives Will Attend

The owners of Wang Yu Tai Tea House, Wang Zhenshi and Zhenhuan brothers were kidnapped by bandits on the same day. Zhenhuan cleverly escaped from the bandits. Zhenshi was taken away. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. After Zhenhuan escaped, two bandits holding Mauser pistols fled, encountered a rickshaw, jumped on the rickshaw, and forced the rickshaw puller to flee towards South Chengdu Road. Constable Nie Dianrong, number 2124, and Patrolman, number 2844, pursued with their revolvers, but because of the distance, they could not catch up immediately. A car happened to pass by, and Constable Nie boarded the car and continued to pursue south along Tongfu Road to Lane 79 of Shengmu Yuan Road in the French Concession. When he was close to the bandits' rickshaw, Constable Nie got out of the car and fired four shots at the bandits. The bandits also returned fire with their Mauser pistols, hitting Constable Nie in the left chest. He fell to the ground. By the time Chinese Constable 2844 arrived, the bandits had disappeared. Examining Constable Nie, he was already dead. He immediately reported to the police station, and Detective Ruan Yao rushed to the scene and carried Constable Nie's body to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. After the bandits killed Constable Nie, they abandoned the rickshaw and continued to flee. When they reached Lane 103 of Beidichen Road, they entered House No. 4 of Zhengyuan Li, seeking refuge. The homeowner, Mrs. Chen He, firmly refused. The bandits then ran through the back door into House No. 9, but were also refused entry by the homeowner, Mrs. Zhang Li. The bandits had no choice but to retreat, abandoning the Mauser pistol in the gutter and fleeing empty-handed. Someone retrieved the abandoned gun and sent it to the French police station. Later, Detective Ruan went to Zhengyuan Li to investigate and found two rows of bullets outside the door of House No. 9. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo of the Special District Local Court went to the scene to examine the body. Detective Ruan recounted the circumstances of the pursuit and investigation. The two fleeing bandits were about five feet seven inches tall, with slightly elongated faces, and were wearing short clothes. Prosecutor Guo then instructed the deceased's wife to sign a statement and claim the body for burial. It is reported that Nie Dianrong was from Yanzhou, Shandong, only twenty-four years old, and lived with his wife at No. 603, Ma'an Li, Chongqing Road. They had two children, both only three or four years old. This time, he bravely pursued the bandits and was killed by them in the line of duty. The police department specially granted a cash compensation of one thousand yuan to support the bereaved family. The funeral will be held tomorrow (Monday). The police chief will issue an order to all Chinese and Western detectives in the police department to attend and offer condolences to show mourning and demonstrate exemplary conduct.

Rickshaw Puller Who Colluded with Kidnappers

Ding Jinfang Executed by Firing Squad Yesterday

Asked Someone to Send a Letter to His Parents to Ease Their Grief

Instructed His Wife to Take Good Care of Their Son and Accumulate Merit

Ding Jinfang (also known as Jinfeng and Afu), a native of Tongzhou, had been hired as a rickshaw puller by Zhou Zongzhi, a Cantonese employee of Hongyu Yarn Factory. On the morning of January 14th of the previous year, Zhou was kidnapped by bandits while riding in Ding's rickshaw from his residence at No. 567, Xin Dagu Road, to the factory. Subsequently, the Public Concession Police cracked the case, rescued Zhou from the bandits' den, and arrested the kidnappers, including Liu Arong, who were duly punished according to the law. Later, it was discovered that Zhou's kidnapping was actually initiated by Ding, who colluded with the kidnappers to betray his employer for money. Ding was arrested and charged according to the law. On November 11th of the previous year, after investigation by the Special District Local Court, he was sentenced to death. The sentence was submitted to and approved by the higher authorities and executed as originally sentenced. Yesterday morning, the Special Court instructed the handling police station to bring Ding from the Western Prison. Judge Cheng Shangfeng took the bench and announced that the death penalty would be carried out. He then asked the prisoner if he had any last words. According to Ding, he was thirty years old, and his parents, wife, and children lived at No. 37, Lujiazhai, Baoshan Road, Zhabei. His father's name was Ding Longxian. Accusing Fuchang's Manager and Huang Chu Jiu's Son

Shanghai South Public Buses Add Longhua Special Bus

From April 1st to May 15th

The Longhua Temple in Shanghai West is said to have been built in the Jin Dynasty. Ascending the ancient pagoda and looking down, one can see people like ants and horses like beans. The breeze carries the sounds of chanting, making one feel refreshed. Every year when the willows turn green and the peach blossoms bloom, many men and women go there together. However, the round trip is dozens of miles, and transportation is not very convenient. The Shanghai South Public Bus Company has decided to add a special bus from April 1st to May 15th, in addition to the original Route 2 public bus, to facilitate spring outings for men and women. The special bus will run directly from the Old West Gate via Xiejiao to Longhua. Each person will be charged 48 copper coins to facilitate round trips for tourists.

Xia Dexing Sand Ship Robbed

Goods Worth a Total of Forty to Fifty Thousand Taels

Captain, Helmsman, and Others Kidnapped

Demand of Six Thousand Silver Dollars for Ransom

Three or Four Crew Members Injured

The Beiyang class sand ship Xia Dexing has always sailed to Yingkou, Dalian, and other ports, specializing in carrying passengers and goods. After the Niuzhuang River froze last winter, it sailed to Qingkou in Shandong Province. Recently, it received a telegram ordering the ship to sail to Niuzhuang because the river was about to thaw. Therefore, the ship loaded cloth, woolen cloth, and other goods worth forty to fifty thousand taels in Shanghai and set sail. Unexpectedly, it encountered several pirate ships in the waters off Haizhou. The pirate ships surrounded the merchant ship and robbed it. When the Xia ship saw this situation, it immediately turned the rudder to retreat. However, it was spotted by the pirates, who immediately opened fire on the Xia ship and chased after it. The pirate ships were smaller and faster, while the Xia ship was heavily loaded and larger, so it was slower. As a result, it was still caught. The pirates, wielding guns, swarmed onto the ship, extremely angry. They indiscriminately attacked people and rushed to the captain's, surnamed Ye, cabin to rob him. They robbed him of more than seven hundred silver dollars, but they were still not satisfied. They insisted on asking where more silver dollars were hidden and demanded that he hand them over immediately. Ye said that this was all he had and that there was no other place where he had hidden silver dollars. The pirates questioned why he had fled. Ye said that he did not know and that it was the helmsman's responsibility. The pirates then kidnapped the captain of the ship, Ye, to the pirate ship. Then they opened the cargo hold and robbed the goods, carrying away more than a hundred pieces of cloth. Before leaving, they kidnapped the helmsman and two crew members and said to the crew that if they wanted to redeem them, they had to prepare six thousand silver dollars within half a month and contact them at the same place. After speaking, they drove the pirate ship away in a hurry, heading towards the northern sea off Haizhou. After the pirates left, the Xia ship sailed to the port of Haizhou and anchored. Three or four crew members were severely injured by the pirates on board and were sent to the hospital for treatment. The ship's hull was also hit by more than a dozen bullets. Yesterday, the ship's accountant came to Shanghai to report to various cargo companies, requesting them to find a way to rescue the kidnapped captain and others. The various cargo companies have telegraphed the local government office to strictly suppress the pirates.

Strange Tales of Healing

Drinking Tea Before the Rain Can Activate Blood Circulation

Bowing to the Sky Can Exercise the Meridians

Recently, two people from Wuxi, Yang Jingan and Yin Xingquan, claiming to be able to cure diseases, have been in House No. 1, Hesheng Li, Wangjia Wharf, Nanshi. They hung a scroll in the middle with the two large characters "Sky" written on it, claiming that they could summon the heavenly generals to cast spells to exorcise disease demons. They muttered incessantly all day long, and rang bells and chimes, making Buddhist sounds that reverberated outside. They also had unemployed people praise their various skills in order to deceive patients and extort money from them. Soon, ignorant men and women believed them and flocked to them. As the news spread, the first precinct and first section of the jurisdiction found out and immediately sent police to arrest Yang and Yin and detain them in the station for preliminary interrogation. According to their confession, they were only treating people for their illnesses and did not charge any money, offering only complete voluntary assistance. They said that difficult and strange diseases arose purely from the patient's blood circulation not being smooth. Therefore, when patients came to the fairy altar they set up, they would first respectfully drink tea before the rain from the top to stimulate their blood circulation, and then make the patients kowtow to the sky to exercise the meridians. After that, they would have them rest quietly for a few minutes, and the illness would be cured immediately. There was no extortion involved. They were ordered to remain in custody for investigation, as they had been engaged in soliciting money under false pretenses for a long time in violation of the ban.

The Shanghai South Public Bus Company's Route 4 bus, which runs between Xujiahui and Hongqiao Airport, has been losing money in recent years due to competition from British public buses, which have been selling tickets at reduced prices. Municipal Authorities Prohibit Fishing Boats and Cargo Ships from Docking at Shanghai South Wharves

Order to Moor at Buoys Set Up by Customs

Many fishing boats and cargo ships dock at the Shanghai South Wharf, hindering the entry and exit of commercial ships. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, at the request of the shipping company, has previously conducted a survey with the Public Security Bureau to determine the mooring locations for fishing boats, etc., and consulted with the Jianghai Customs to add two buoys for mooring. The joint notice from the Public Utilities and Public Security Bureaus prohibiting fishing boats, etc., from docking at the wharves is recorded as follows:

Notice of Joint Prohibition: The Shanghai South Municipal Wharves are all for commercial ships traveling to and from the coast, the Yangtze River, and inland rivers. The entry and exit are frequent. If other ships are allowed to stay arbitrarily in front of the wharves, it will greatly hinder the entry and exit of the commercial ships and cause many collisions. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau previously reported that there were often fishing boats, etc., staying in front of the wharves. The Jianghai Customs has long set up buoys in the Jiangnan River in Shanghai for cargo ships and fishing boats to moor. Now, two more buoys will be added in addition to the original buoys. All cargo ships and fishing boats should moor at the buoys and not stay arbitrarily in front of the wharves, hindering the entry and exit of commercial ships. This notice is hereby issued jointly. All cargo ships and fishing boats must be informed that if they stay arbitrarily in front of the wharves again, the Public Security Bureau will severely punish them and will not tolerate them. It is important to abide by this notice.

Municipal Public Utilities Bureau Issues Rules for Privately Owned Public Utility Vehicles

Recently, various universities and other institutions in the city have increasingly owned privately owned public utility vehicles, and the consumption of gasoline and other items is very large. Some charge students, teachers, and staff for rides. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau believes that the sale of tickets along the way is close to business operations, which conflicts with the rights already obtained by commercial public bus companies, and that the structure of these vehicles carrying many passengers is also closely related to public safety. Therefore, it has drafted 13 rules for prohibition and submitted them to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgation as follows:

Shanghai Municipal Rules for Prohibiting Privately Owned Public Utility Vehicles Charging Fees

Article 1: All institutions in the city that own privately owned public utility vehicles and charge fees shall be governed by these rules.

Article 2: Any institution that wishes to own such vehicles shall first specify the route and stopping points in writing and request a license from the Public Utilities Bureau.

Article 3: If the route of the vehicle is within the business scope of a commercially operated public bus company, the company should first be given the opportunity to operate the route. If the company is unwilling to do so, the vehicle-owning institution may operate the route, and both parties shall submit a joint report to the Public Utilities Bureau for record.

Article 4: The vehicle-owning institution shall submit the vehicle's chassis, body, and drawings to the Public Utilities Bureau for approval before it can be manufactured.

Article 5: After the vehicle has been inspected and approved by the Public Utilities Bureau, it shall pay taxes at the same rate as commercial vehicles.

Article 6: The passengers carried by the vehicle shall be limited to internal personnel of the institution.

Article 7: The amount of fees charged by the vehicle shall be determined within the scope of gasoline and other consumption expenses and reported to the Public Utilities Bureau in writing for record. It shall not be for profit.

Article 8: The fees charged by the vehicle shall be limited to the originally designated route.

Article 9: The fee collection method for the vehicle shall be to exchange for a ride pass within the institution. Tickets shall not be sold along the way or on the vehicle. The sample of the ride pass shall be submitted to the Public Utilities Bureau for record after it is determined.

Article 10: In addition to the provisions of this chapter, all other rules and regulations regarding private vehicles shall be followed.

Article 11: Anyone who violates any of the following articles shall be dealt with in accordance with the regulations, and the Public Utilities Bureau may revoke the vehicle's license at any time.

Article 12: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any omissions.

Article 13: These rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Daughter Who Has Married is Having an Affair

A'Xin, daughter of Zhou Huoxiang, a farmer residing in the Zhou Wang family compound in Hongqiao Township, Shanghai West, is a beautiful twenty-five-year-old woman with a modern bobbed hairstyle. Last autumn, she married Huo Sheng, daughter of Wang Xingquan from Xinqiao nearby, through a matchmaker. Initially, the couple's relationship was excellent, but later, disagreements arose due to minor family matters. A'Xin then returned to her mother's home. Soon after, she became romantically involved with a man named Xue and lived with him secretly in the Jing'an Temple Road area. The day before yesterday afternoon, Xue's friend, Xu Yulin, accompanied Zhou's daughter to a dowry shop on Hongqiao Road to purchase tables and chairs. They were spotted by Wang's relatives, who detained the man and woman. After mediation, Xu paid a ransom of forty yuan before being released. It is now reported that the Wang family has accused Xue in the District Court of enticing their child to elope, while the Xu family has reported Wang Xingquan to the relevant police station for allegedly colluding with hooligans to extort money under false pretenses.

The Jianquan Taijiquan Association was founded by renowned martial arts masters Wu Jianquan, Chu Minyi, Xu Zhiyi, and others. Case of Japanese Car Killing Ningbo Native

Japanese Consulate Responds to Mayor Zhang

Chen Jinguan, a native of Ningbo, was struck and killed by car number 2343 while walking on Huade Road. The car is owned by Japanese merchant Morimura's car dealership, and the driver was a Japanese man named Yoshioka. Chen's family reported the incident through the Shanghai Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association, which requested the municipal government to negotiate with the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai. The Japanese Consulate General has now responded to Mayor Zhang, stating that the driver will only be detained for fifty days and that the car owner, Morimura, is willing to offer about fifty yuan to comfort the bereaved family. Mayor Zhang has already forwarded the letter to the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association for their information.

Truck Carrying Goods Collides With Utility Pole

Avoiding a Child Prevents Fatality

Violent Collision Damages the Vehicle

Yesterday afternoon, at around 4:00 PM, a truck with municipal license plate number 3605, carrying a large batch of approximately one hundred parcels from Zhenru, was traveling east on Zhongxing Road, in front of the Taiyuanfang area of Zhabei, heading to the General Post Office to send them to various provinces. Unexpectedly, at that location, Rong Sheng, an eight-year-old child of Zhu Zhoufa from Nantong, who lives nearby at 29 Fanli, and works pushing a cart at a soap factory, was playing in the road with a girl. The driver of the truck, Zhu Rongqing, also from Nantong, in an attempt to avoid the girl, turned the front of the truck south. Rong Sheng was knocked down by the mudguard of the truck and fell underneath it. Because the truck was overloaded, it had double wheels on the back. The child was caught between the wheels, but fortunately, pole number 84 on the side of the road stopped the truck from crashing violently into the cement base of the pole. The front of the truck was severely damaged, and the electrical wires were severed. The child was lucky to survive, suffering only minor facial injuries. Without the pole to stop it, the child would likely have died. Police officers arrived at the scene and took the driver and the injured child to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau. It was discovered that the injured child had been in Shanghai for less than a month and was unaware of the dangers of traffic on the road. The damaged truck belongs to Jiuda Automobile Company on North Shaanxi Road and Avenue Edward VII in the British Concession and is contracted to transport mail for the Zhenru Post Office.

Girl Run Over and Killed by Bus

Yu Guixing, the nine-year-old daughter of Yu Pengfei, a local resident living at number 12 Fudeli, on the east side of Shafei Road and Songshan Road in the French Concession, was a student at Chongzhen Elementary School in Yudeli, Route Cardinal Foch. Yesterday, near noon, during lunchtime, Guixing and two male classmates left Yudeli to buy food across the street. The two boys were in front, and Guixing was behind. As they were crossing the road, a French-owned bus, number 820, traveling from east to west, passed by. The two boys in front managed to avoid it, but Guixing was unable to get out of the way and was struck, suffering injuries to her head, left cheek, chest, and back. She immediately lost consciousness. Police officers recorded the license plate number and transported the injured person and the bus to Renji Hospital. Due to the severity of her injuries, she died at 2:00 PM. The hospital notified the police station, which transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for examination.

Fine for Car Dealerships Failing to Affix Stamp Duty

Since the Ministry of Finance established a special stamp duty office in the Shanghai Concession and strictly enforced the affixing of stamp duty, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Taxpayers Association, and other organizations have repeatedly issued notices and urged businesses to respect national taxes and comply with regulations. In cases where stamp duty is not affixed to invoices and account books, people are allowed to report the violations, and the courts will issue summons for punishment. Recently, Weihai Automobile Company on Weihaiwei Road and Jiujiang Automobile Company on Jiujiang Road have been found to have failed to affix stamp duty to their car licenses and business account books. On the 20th of this month, the court issued search warrants, and the office dispatched personnel along with detectives from the police station to search the premises. At Jiujiang Automobile Company, they discovered one account book without stamp duty, and at Weihai Automobile Company, they found two account books without stamp duty. This morning, Judge Tao of the court held a hearing and ordered Jiujiang Automobile Company to pay a fine of thirty yuan and Weihai Automobile Company to pay a fine of twenty-five yuan. He also instructed them to affix stamp duty to all documents in accordance with regulations in the future. The car dealerships paid the fines and complied with the court's instructions.

Killed in Revenge Attack

Five Gunshot Wounds to Waist, Ribs, and Chest

It was reported yesterday that Pang Gongyi, a former detective of the Third Water Police Team residing at 39 Zhongxingli, Hongzhen, was shot and killed. It has now been learned that the incident was a complete revenge killing, as the assailant only targeted the victim. The Fifth District Third Precinct has dispatched police to investigate the case and has also submitted a report to the Public Security Bureau to request the dispatch of detectives for the apprehension of the perpetrator. Yesterday, Xu Jinlin, the head of the 15th Tu of the 27th Bao, reported the incident to the District Court for examination. Prosecutor Yang and others were assigned to the scene and found five gunshot wounds to the waist, ribs, and chest. They determined that the death was caused by the injuries and filled out an autopsy report. During the inquiry, the victim's wife claimed that a total of ten shots were fired, with five hitting the victim. Zhu Ziqiao Telegrams About His Whereabouts

Tianchu MSG Sold to Aid Disaster Relief

The Shanghai Temporary Relief Committee for Shaanxi Disaster Relief received a telegram from Zhu Ziqiao yesterday, stating that he had arrived in Ji'nan and was staying at the Jiaoji Hotel and would go to Tianjin in the evening. He will come to Shanghai after finishing his business there. The committee sent a letter to the Shanghai Office of the National Government Relief Committee yesterday, stating that Mr. Zhu Ziqiao came to Shanghai from afar to solicit donations for Shaanxi disaster relief, which is particularly severe and short of funds. He has now raised 100 boxes of Tianchu MSG, which will be shipped to Shaanxi for sale to provide relief funds. The goods will be shipped from Shanghai to Tianjin by sea today and then transferred to Beijing, where Mr. Zhu Ziqiao will transfer them via the Pinghan and Longhai railways to Shaanxi. The committee requested that the National Government Relief Committee forward the request to the Ministry of Finance for the issuance of a tax-exempt passport from Shanghai to Shaanxi for inspection and release along the way. It also requested that China Merchants Steam Navigation Company be authorized to provide free shipping from Shanghai to Tianjin to save on transportation costs and reduce relief expenses.

Appeal for Disaster Relief from Anhui

Please Grant Relief Quickly

The Chinese Red Cross recently received a telegram from the Sixian Disaster Relief Committee of Anhui, stating that Sixian has been plagued by natural disasters and man-made calamities in recent years. In the summer of the 17th year, the Yu bandits led by Li Laomo burned down dozens of wealthy shops in urban and rural areas, raping, killing, and looting, leaving ruins everywhere. Before the people could recover, they were hit by a severe drought in the 18th year, resulting in a complete failure of the wheat and autumn harvests. The people were starving and crying for food. Taking advantage of the situation, bandits gathered in the eastern part of the county, kidnapping, stealing cattle, and extorting money from the people. At the same time, the communists carried out brutal acts in the western mountains, killing, burning, and forming so-called Red Guards and assassination squads, sparing no one who resisted them. The southwestern half of the county became a terrifying place. For months, the people could neither live nor die. Fortunately, the National Army and local security forces worked hard to suppress the eastern bandits, and the western communists were also driven out. However, last December, the evil communists launched a full-scale invasion from the border of Hubei, numbering more than 20,000, and successively captured several towns, including Jinjiazhai, Liubo Village, Mabao, Dushan, and Subao, and marched straight to the city. The disaster area covered more than 200 miles, and less than 100,000 people fled to the city with their families, young and old. In the freezing weather, they were displaced, relying on nothing, exposed to the wind and rain, and suffering from starvation. They were on the verge of death. The local organizations urgently formed a disaster relief committee and set up refugee camps. They requested the provincial government to issue 3,000 yuan for emergency relief and raised donations locally to provide relief. However, this was only a drop in the bucket. Moreover, the communists were still entrenched in the western mountains, and it was unknown when they would be defeated. If relief is not provided quickly, the refugees, young and old, will fill the ditches and die. Furthermore, on February 15th, the soldiers of the 272nd Regiment of the Sixth Defense Army suddenly rebelled in Liucheng, and shops and residents throughout the city were looted. The impact was devastating and unprecedented. The Sixian region is under threat from bandits and communists, and even the central area is not safe. Thousands of merchants and residents have become destitute, heavily indebted, and unable to do business. The city is in decline, and the sight is heartbreaking. The undersigned appeal to all kind-hearted people to extend their compassion and provide grain and aid quickly. If you can help more, you can save more lives. The relief efforts will be remembered forever. We express our urgent plea with tears. Sincerely, The Sixian Disaster Relief Committee, Standing Committee Members: Weng Qianshui, Cui Yaohua, Chao Yangzhi, Shao Mengjue, Zhou Ziqian, Cheng Yicheng, Yang Shiru.

Commissioner Guan Reviews the Daji Wheel Case

Tax Commissioner May Responds to the Ship

Structure is Solid, Management is Appropriate

Regarding the fire on the Dada Company's Shanghai-Yangzhou route Daji Wheel on the 11th of this month near Longju Sand, Tongzhou, which resulted in the tragic deaths of more than two hundred crew members and passengers and the loss of cargo, the Ministry of Transportation telegraphed the Jianghai Customs Commissioner to investigate the cause of the fire, the number of casualties, and to instruct the company to quickly devise a plan for handling the aftermath. Commissioner Liu appointed Tang Naigen as a committee member to conduct a detailed investigation of the company and instructed Dada Company to quickly submit a report on how they will handle the casualties, compensation, and other matters. Commissioner Liu also sent a letter to Jianghai Customs Tax Commissioner May, instructing him to investigate whether the structure and management of the Daji Wheel were appropriate and to report back for further action. As time has passed, the Commissioner's office has urged Dada Company to submit a detailed report on how they will handle compensation. Yesterday, Dada Company manager Bao Chengpei sent a representative, Mr. Wang, to the Commissioner's office to meet with Secretary Xu and submit a report stating that all matters related to compensation and handling of the aftermath for the Daji Wheel will be handled in accordance with maritime law. However, most of the families of the victims are poor, and the company has already purchased coffins for the victims and is gradually providing compensation. Once this is completed, a report will be submitted. The Commissioner's office has reportedly submitted a report on the investigation to the Ministry of Transportation for review. Jianghai Customs Tax Commissioner May, after receiving the Commissioner's request to investigate whether the structure and management of the Daji Wheel were complete and appropriate, responded that the structure of the Daji Wheel was very solid and perfect, and the management was appropriate and did not violate the regulations of maritime navigation.

Wu Wenhua Ordered to Thoroughly Investigate the Daji Wheel Tragedy

The Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department is paying close attention to the case of the Dada Company's Daji Wheel fire, which resulted in the deaths of three or four hundred passengers. The Shanghai-Yangzhou route operated by the company is essential for north-south transportation and passenger safety. This unprecedented tragedy indicates that the ship's management was negligent and lacked proper precautions. A thorough investigation is necessary. Therefore, Director Sun instructed Wu Wenhua, director of the Shanghai County Construction Bureau, yesterday to conduct a thorough investigation of the victims, Dada Company, and other relevant parties to provide a detailed report for review.

According to the Shanghai South Society, Qin Xitian, director of the Shanghai County Public Funds and Property Department, has served in his position for more than ten years. Labor Dispute at the Guangdong Brothers Rubber Factory Resolved

On February 5th, the Guangdong Brothers Rubber Factory on Weituoma Road announced changes to the employee leave system, which the workers opposed, leading to a labor dispute. The factory fired nine workers, including the leader, Bai Zongxi, and reported them to the police for arrest. The workers had no choice but to request assistance from the Social Affairs Bureau. After repeated mediation by the bureau, no results were achieved. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the fourth mediation was convened, with Liang Pinqing and Pang Ziqing representing the employer and Bai Zongxi and others representing the employees. After a long discussion led by Chairman Wang Bing, the representatives of both parties agreed to sign a three-article agreement: (1) The factory is allowed to dismiss the nine workers, including A'Lin. (2) The factory will pay each of the above workers 46 yuan. (3) The factory will immediately request the police to drop the case against Bai Zongxi and others.

Taixing Sends Representatives to Shanghai for Disaster Relief

Taixing was originally a wealthy area, but in the past three years, bandits and communists have risen up, and villages have been destroyed. Some families of dozens of people have been slaughtered, leaving only one or two survivors, and even those survivors have been killed. The stench of blood filled the air, and the ground was scorched. The total loss is estimated at more than 50 million yuan. Although the suppression has been completed, the vitality of the area has been greatly damaged. People have been displaced, and many have starved to death on the road. Recently, Dai Weifu and others from the Taixing County Disaster Relief Association came to Shanghai and have been begging for aid from all sides. It is reported that they have received the support of many philanthropists.

High-Quality Domestically Produced Pencils Arrive in Shanghai

Produced by Baoxing Minerals Factory

The Baoxing Mineral Powder Factory, located at the intersection of Zhongxing Road and Baochang Road in Zhabei, operates a pencil mine in the Xiashu Town of Jurong County, Jiangsu Province, near Shijian Mountain. Although the mine is still in the exploratory stage and a mine bed is being constructed, mining has been progressing smoothly. Approximately 200 tons of ore have been transported to Shanghai. Testing has shown that the ore is of high quality and suitable for manufacturing dry batteries, stoves, ink pencils, paint, and casting sand. At the beginning of this month, Dr. Shen Xiongqing, director of the Industrial Goods Testing Institute of the Social Affairs Bureau, and Hu Guoguang, director of the Telecommunications Machinery Manufacturing Factory of the Ministry of Transportation, visited the factory and praised it highly.

Detectives from the French Concession Police Department discovered that residents of Bao Linhe's home were operating a private gambling den, gathering people to gamble and taking a cut for profit, which violated the prohibition. They raided the place the night before last, seizing gambling equipment and gambling money and arresting more than ten gamblers. The detectives first reported the previous situation to the court. Bao confessed to operating a private gambling den and taking a cut. Seizure of Smuggled Opium

At around 10:00 PM the night before last, Liu, a clerk from the First Squad of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, received a report from detectives Yang Chunting and Wang Weiheng that the Dalian Maru steamship, which was docked at the Huangpu Wharf, was smuggling opium. Liu dispatched officers, including Lu Songxing, to patrol the area around the wharf. At around 1:00 AM yesterday, the officers spotted a man standing on the wharf, acting suspiciously. They approached him and searched him, finding a paper package containing twelve pieces of opium, weighing approximately 140 taels. They arrested the man and brought him back to the squad, then transferred him to the Nanshi General Squad. Chief Xu preliminarily questioned the man, who identified himself as Chang Ren, 28 years old, from Ganyu. He said that Liu, who worked in the stokehold of the Dalian Maru steamship, had asked him to deliver the opium to the ship. He was charged with carrying prohibited goods and ordered to submit a statement to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Zhang Weiquan Fined and Released

Zhang Weiquan, a director from the Zhangjiabang Maijiazhai in Pudong, was accused of illegal activities by more than sixty local residents at the Public Security Bureau. When the Public Security Bureau sent police to arrest him, Zhang was found lying in bed smoking opium. He and the opium paraphernalia were seized. The Public Security Bureau transferred him to the District Court, which sentenced him to a fine of 100 yuan for the opium offense. The remaining charges were not tried. Zhang has now paid the fine and been released.

Fine of 300 Yuan for Carrying Red Pills

Chen Wenzeng was found carrying a package of red pills while passing through the French Concession. The police arrested Chen and seized the red pills. Yesterday, he was sent to the French Court for investigation. The police reported the previous situation and presented the red pills to the court. Chen confessed that a friend had asked him to deliver the red pills to a certain place. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced Chen to a fine of 300 yuan, confiscated the red pills, and ordered them to be destroyed.

Memorial Service for Han's Mother Today

Mrs. Shen, the mother of Judge Han Zuzhi of the Civil Division of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, passed away. Han summoned his pure filial piety and grieved deeply. The memorial service will be held today (Sunday) at the Puyi Agency on Guling Road. Relatives, friends, and former and current colleagues who heard the news sent their condolences. Today, those who come to pay their respects are particularly numerous. Xu Weizhen, president of the High Court Branch, Yang Zhaoxun, president of the Special Zone Court, and the chiefs of the civil and criminal divisions of the two courts, judges, prosecutors, secretaries, and section chiefs of the two courts will all personally attend the memorial service. The hearse and white horses will be magnificent. The funeral is scheduled to be held on the fifth of the next month.

Peder's High Quality Domestically Produced Neckties Launched in Bulk

Recently, with gold prices soaring and foreign goods skyrocketing, Peder's launched a large number of domestically produced spring ties, with many colors and patterns and prices half that of foreign goods. They are now available at Daqingli on Nanjing Road and 91 Sichuan Road.

China's Journalism to be Republished

China's Journalism is a masterpiece carefully crafted by Mr. Huang Tianpeng. Since its publication, it has been popular in China. The journalism departments of Shanghai Fudan University and Beijing Yenching University have adopted it as a textbook or key reference book. The first edition is about to be sold out, and the author is currently revising and expanding the content. In addition to the general theory, origin, evolution, current status, and future of Chinese journalism, and the national newspaper directory, a new chapter on "The Newspaper Industry in the Last One or Two Years" has been added. The entire book contains 300,000 words and is a grand spectacle in the academic world. The Joint Bookstore is currently holding a major sale, selling the remaining copies of the first edition at a discount of 80%.

Henry Tuxedos Available for Rent at Affordable Prices

Henry Tailor Company, located at 7 Westward Road, has newly made a large number of men's and women's wedding suits and hats with new styles and durable materials, which have always been praised by people from all walks of life. In order to give preferential treatment to customers, the rental price is especially cheap. Branches are located on Nanjing Road, Sichuan Road, Jing'an Temple and other places.

China Business Company recently completed a major real estate transaction this week. The property is reportedly located in the eastern district and covers approximately 300 mu, with an investment of approximately 5 million taels.

Tenants of Guangxing Lane Oppose Rent Increase

The tenants of Guangxing Lane in Hongkou, alarmed and disoriented by a notice issued on March 25th by the landlord, Shanghai Bank, proposing to increase the monthly rent from $28.30 to $75.80, an increase of as much as 30%, reported in groups to the Tenants' Association. The association convened an emergency meeting yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. More than 30 tenants attended, including Chen Yanru and Yang Guoxian. Chairman Tang Huilian conducted the meeting with due ceremony. The chairman announced the purpose of the meeting, followed by resolutions on the following items: (1) Regarding the method of dealing with the rent increase, a unanimous decision was made to reject it and to send a letter to the landlord requesting understanding of the difficulties of business and a swift withdrawal of the order. (2) It was decided to increase the number of temporary propagandists by adding Guan Ruisheng, Wencheng Hao, Guangfa, Chen Yanru, and Yang Guoxian, a total of five people. (3) A petition will be submitted to the Municipal Government to uphold justice. (4) Economic issues will be handled by the Executive Committee. (5) Other motions were discussed until the meeting adjourned at 6 p.m.

She was sent to the Xinpu Nursery for care and an advertisement was placed to find her family.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the sky is cloudy. There is fog in the Yangtze River basin and along the coast here in the morning. There is a cyclone in Liaodong due to a low-pressure system passing through the northern region and moving eastward. The wind on the Yellow Sea and East Sea is gentle and undirected. Also, in the 24 hours before 2 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 66.0 degrees and the lowest was 41.2 degrees. At the same time last year, the highest was 68.0 degrees and the lowest was 55.7 degrees.

Free Talk

World Tidbits

— Sea Guest

▲ A professor at the University of London said that the world's culture really originated in Egypt. It is wrong for people to say that numbers originated in Babylonia.

▲ Because many dance halls in Paris do not follow the rules of dancing, such as intimate embraces, which are harmful to public morals, the local authorities want to manufacture a special belt so that men and women cannot stick together when dancing. Another type of buffer is made so that faces cannot stick together either.

▲ Mrs. Williams of Carmarthenshire, England, married in 1883 and gave birth to a son before she was seventeen. Fifteen years later, her son married and had a child, making her a grandmother at the age of thirty-one. The British consider this a remarkable event.

▲ Dockworkers in Dunkirk, northern France, initiated a competition to carry heavy objects. One person carried 716 pounds of heavy objects for 13 yards and won the victory.

▲ A beekeeping expert in England started beekeeping in 1865. Twenty years later, his business became very successful, supplying honey to 5,000 people in the town. He accumulated 200,000 pounds when he died and was known as the "Honey King."

▲ Several large-scale thief gangs in England hire extremely skilled blacksmiths and coppersmiths at high wages to specialize in making various burglary tools, which are extremely ingenious.

Ten Thousand People Commemorate Huanghuagang Today

— Zizai

The annual Huanghuagang commemoration is once again before our eyes. President Sun regarded the martyrs of this uprising as having great significance, saying, "This battle gathered the elite of revolutionary parties from various provinces to fight to the last with the Manchus. Although the event did not succeed, the heroic spirit of the 72 martyrs of Huanghuagang shook the world, and the domestic revolutionary situation was indeed created." In this battle, the blood flowed freely and the heroic spirit filled the air. The long-dormant hearts of the people across the country were greatly excited, and the accumulated resentment was like a torrent that could not be restrained. In less than half a year, the great revolution of Wuchang was successful, so the value of this battle is truly significant and great."

Huanghuagang was originally named Honghuagang. Initially, Pan Dawei collected and buried the bodies of the party members, not wanting to publicize it. Unexpectedly, the next day, the royalist newspaper Guoshi Bao first published an article with unfavorable words about Pan. Pan knew it was difficult to hide the truth, so he announced the whole story, with the headline "New Ghost Records Before the Consultative Bureau, Martyr Monument on Huanghuagang." The intention was to use the two characters "Honghua" (red flower) to indicate weakness, not knowing the vigorousness of "Huanghua" (yellow flower). The newspapers followed suit, and the name has become established ever since.

The most powerful recruiters for the Guangzhou Revolution on March 29th of the Xinhai year were Zhu Zhixin and Zou Haibin. Those who managed the cemetery were Lin Zichao (Sen) and Fang Yun Song (Shengtao). Among the 72 martyrs examined, the youngest was Yu Dongxiong, only 18 years old, and the oldest was Huang Bingzhong, 45 years old. Most of them were between 20 and 30 years old. In terms of provincial籍, Guangdong accounted for 41 people, Fujian 19, Guangxi 6, and Sichuan and Anhui 3 each. By county, Huaxian accounted for 18 people. By surname, the surname Xu accounted for 16 people.

The commander-in-chief of this battle was Zhao Sheng, and the deputy commander was Huang Xing. Both escaped to Hong Kong. In March of the first year of the Republic, Huang Keqiang wrote a eulogy for the Huanghuagang public memorial: "Seventy-two brave men fought fiercely in the spring clouds and soaked in azure blood; four hundred million countrymen sadly watch the autumn rain wet the yellow flowers." There is also a poem in the tune of "Butterflies Lingering Over Flowers" mourning Huanghuagang: "In the blink of an eye, the yellow flowers are blooming. I ask the west wind to temporarily cover the fragrance, waiting for the branches to be full of fresh dew and fragrance, blowing on the ruthless tomb. Looking back on Guangzhou in March, blood and flesh flew, and the spirit swallowed the fierce captives. Failure or success are originally rat-like, and heroes are silent underground." The matter belongs to personal experience and is expressed in poetic beauty. The words here cannot be created by those who merely search for chapters and sentences.

On March 14th of the twelfth year of the Republic, Yu Youren and Deng Yun, Zili, and others visited Huanghuagang and met Lin Zichao, writing a poem: "The sun is setting below Baiyun Mountain, sweeping the tomb and meeting you with added emotion. It is said that after the spring rain, plant yellow flowers on Huanghuagang." He also visited the tomb of the 72 martyrs of Huanghuagang with Zeng Mengming, writing a poem: "Below Huanghuagang, we step and wipe our handkerchiefs. It is difficult for those who die later to respectfully present the tombs of the former sages. We made the same oath in those years, and today we envy their success. Pick the seeds of cockscomb flowers and send them to the Minzhi campus" (picking cockscomb flower seeds to send to the Minzhi campus). I also wrote a eulogy for the Huanghuagang memorial, which is recorded below to express my grief. The eulogy reads: "Sacrificing blood to exchange for the republic, lightly risking life, throwing heads, and grieving that you generously sacrificed your lives. Tragically buried heroic bones by the city's edge, contemplating the yellow flowers and thinking of the former martyrs, preparing the heart and bowing respectfully. Ashamed of us who live in ease and have not died, we come to the hill to mourn the heroic souls." Being a member of the People's Party, I cannot continue the legacy of the martyrs, and I am grieved by the departed and ashamed of myself.

Prelude to the Direct Flight of Eurasia Aviation

— Wang Meiju

On the 16th of this month, Mr. Sun Mutang, Secretary of the Board of Directors of Eurasia Aviation, invited me to the Hongqiao Airport to see the company's two new test flight aircraft, and to meet the company's gentlemen at the office on the third floor of No. 25 Renji Road. After being shown the articles of association, we had a pleasant conversation before parting. Nowadays, the aviation industry is expanding day by day. The company is a joint venture between the Chinese Ministry of Communications and the German Lufthansa. China accounts for two-thirds and Germany one-third of the capital. The organization is well-funded and well-organized. I will record what I saw and heard at the time of the visit, as well as what Mr. Sun has told me in the past one or two days, as a prelude to the direct flight of Eurasia Aviation.

▲ The enthusiasm for the visit: During the visit, Chinese and foreign people crowded the station. When the plane circled and took off, there was thunderous applause and the order was orderly. However, this was only the first of the test flights, only to Beijing Nanyuan. Mr. Sun said that the official inaugural flight will be at the beginning of next month, flying directly from Shanghai to Berlin. At that time, the visit will be even more enthusiastic.

▲ The meticulous organization: The company has a general manager, a board of directors, and several secretaries. The office is divided into three groups: operations, finance, and aviation. The shares are under the jurisdiction of each group to serve. Externally, the stations along the aviation line are divided into first and second class, with directors and other staff. The number of Chinese staff is two-thirds and German staff one-third. There are no biases in obligations and rights.

▲ The novelty of the logo: The company's duty is aviation, flying ten thousand miles in the blue sky and white sun. The logo is a kite flying. Soaring into the unknown and being stable, it is taken as a sign. It can be said to be unique from the Chinese Airlines logo, which uses an eagle.

▲ The instructive nature of fame: Mr. Sun and I are close friends and have only recently met. He is rich in age, strong in talent, careful in mind, and once served as a Cuban consul. His footprints are all over the Atlantic and he is proficient in various languages. He also paints and can create thousands of hills and valleys on a small piece of paper. I was somewhat regretful that he is now working as the secretary of the Board of Directors. Mr. Sun said, "Yesterday I was a head of state, today I am a laborer. This is the true spirit of European democracy. Why should I be reluctant?" I was enlightened and respectfully recorded it.

▲ The remarkable results: Mr. Sun told me that the test flight on the 16th took 6 hours and 15 minutes to reach Beijing Nanyuan. The climate along the way changed a lot, but the machine parts were not affected in any way. The other two aircraft will also be completed within a few days. In the future, it will take at most four days to fly to Berlin, but before the restoration of Russian relations, it will take seven or eight days to connect by train midway.

Jing Shan Photography Society Returns

— Ke Ding'an

My old friend Mr. Lang Jingshan is known for his photography skills, and everyone knows him. There seems to be no need for me to say more. What is described here is what I admire in my heart. When Jingshan was a child, he was diligent in this art. His works were always remarkable and were highly praised by his painting teachers. Because of this, he worked even harder, with a camera never leaving his side. What his eyes and mind touched was immediately captured by the lens and displayed on paper. His fame today is not without reason. Three years ago, he and Hu Boxiang, Zhang Zhenhou, and others formed the Hua Society and publicly exhibited the results of their research at the Shibao Museum. This has been done several times since then.

Recently, at the request of colleagues in the art world, Jing opened a photography studio at No. 1 Beisichuan Lane, North Sichuan Road, and attached a solo exhibition for art lovers to appreciate. I visited Jingshan last night and he happened to be meeting with Tan, discussing various arrangements with great interest. The furnishings were trending towards three-dimensional construction. The tables, chairs, lamps, and sofas all showed new ideas, weeding out old trends. The arrangement of the photography studio was even more artistic, and the beauty of the background and the harmony of the colors gave people a sense of beauty. Jingshan told me that this background is changed every day to avoid the drawbacks of dullness. These words are true. Compared with the photography studios on the market that stick to the old methods, there is no comparison. Even those who usually use art photography to attract customers are very different from Jingshan. Besides taking pictures, photography should also pay attention to the softness and hardness of the light, the selection and abandonment of composition, and the quality of retouching and developing. You must know that the creation of a single piece is not easy, how can the people of the market fully understand it? Looking at the works as a whole, there are no less than hundreds of pieces of portraits, landscapes, still lifes, etc., which have been almost completely collected. The light and composition are just right. Jingshan, in addition to clarifying the essence of the art, has also erected a unique banner. Later, I read the criticism manual and found that famous people such as Chu Minyi, Gan Naiguang, Xu Zhimo, Chen Xiaodie, and Huang Jingwan all had inscriptions, and their words were very pertinent. Jingshan asked me to write a comment, but I had nothing to say. I wrote "The two words 'divine and wonderful' are attributed to it, and I think it can describe Jingshan," and Jingshan smiled at this.

▲ Short News: The Shiyu Lianhuan Society has been established for more than a month. It is now scheduled to hold its first tea party at the society at 2 pm on Sunday, the 29th of this month. Famous people will be invited to give lectures, and visitors from all walks of life are welcome. (Gu Ziyan)

▲ Correction: In the annotatons on "A Painful Word from Huanglu" the previous day, in the eighth line, "suo suo" should be "ci suo" and in the tenth line, "xiu zhi" should be "fu zhi." We hereby correct it.

Feeling and Gifting Butterfly After Watching the Opera Singer Red Peony Movie

— Ye Zhongling

The beauty Butterfly is famous in the South, and her predecessor must be a palace skirt. Her beauty is subtle and without restraint. Her eyebrows are lightly painted like the third month, and the silver screen is lifted and her fame spreads. Flying to the sky, I wish for a bright star, writing the eternal hatred of Han Ping, and the illusionary soul also conveys the love of the Xie family. Who knows that the rouge on the Qin Terrace is re-transmitted, and the Phoenix's son can cry sadly and tightly. Flowers are suitable for thin lives, forgiving the east wind. People are like the setting sun, sad for the evening scenery. In the vast sky, I watch Red Peony. In the season when the red is bustling, I hold a colorful crown. The palace makeup is in Yanzhi Fortress, and the chivalrous bones are sour in the blue mud. The amorous guests are like butterflies fluttering in the wind. Ten dans of bright pearls cannot measure them. The pear garden has a younger brother, a crazy bee, secretly peeping at the jade slave's waist, which is one foot. Mother is afraid of the partridge flying south, advising her son to avoid the golden husband at all costs. She directly teaches the country to be without happy dreams, and even makes the love field a place of complaint. The absurd ten-string song is mistakenly sung, and the concubine's body has been transformed into a tree that shakes. Glimpses of the old jade pendant on her chest, and a mouthful of red clouds makes Etai fall. Her sick wings are difficult to fly, what can she do? The dance clothes are snatched and set off a storm, and there is no son to play with, only a spoiled daughter. Who else will pity the remaining grandmother? She has just left the medicine jar, and the sandalwood clappers cannot bear to fall, rolling down the slope. The people of Ba sing the songs of the Lower Village on a red carpet, and the gyrfalcons and soldiers all roll their eyes. After stopping singing and returning, she loses her palm pearl. A-Xiang cries out her little name. Once the call for chicks enters the market, the fire of the bird cage burns the ladder to call the crows. Iron shoes break through and search in vain, how can she bear Ju Bu's arrival? She is late to the stage with her phoenix hair combed, and her rhinoceros heart is shattered when she hears the drums in chaos. From then on, she endures hunger and cold, and she is also shocked that her husband is heavily tied. Killing people is no better than throwing fish into a net, selling daughters only to know they are entering a phoenix nest. She cries while pulling her clothes in the cave of bewilderment, and she is not allowed to redeem Wenji with empty hands. It is difficult to meet an old acquaintance with lowered eyebrows. Generously waving money to complete the bones and flesh, she examines the cloud clothes and goes to the sea mountain. She sheds tears when she meets her lover, and the soul is lost outside the railing, comforting her feelings. It is difficult to part with the past in front of the car, and ordinary tragedies exist in the world, making my intestines twist. I am willing to bow my head and this is the first sound of China. May you be the only one to walk after Jenny, regretting that the mandarin ducks are flying in opposite directions. Trying to listen from across the forest is not as good as returning home. The pink clothes are not necessarily frivolous, enduring to chase the willow catkins to other branches.

Travel Notes in India (8)

— Linghua

Daojie Shi told me that there is a big problem, which is the Great Treasure Pagoda in Bodh Gaya. According to Dao Shi's estimation, the construction cost of this pagoda should be more than one million rupees. There is a stone tablet in it with Chinese characters recording that Emperor Renzong of the Song Dynasty built it for his father, Emperor Taizong, at the decree of the Empress Dowager. The person in charge was a monk, and it took three years to complete. Dao Shi had taken 100 rubbings of the inscription for examination. If so, it would be a great feat for China to have such a grand building in the Western Regions in the pre-communication era, which would be enough to show the development of our nation's overseas undertakings and not be unworthy of being the Emperor of China. However, Master Wanhui doubts that this pagoda was not built by the Chinese, but that the pagoda built by the Chinese is the small pagoda next to the big pagoda. However, if it is a small pagoda, it would take three years to build. Considering the time spent, it is undoubtedly a large pagoda. Master Wanhui suspects that the pagoda was built by King Ashoka, but Dao Shi refuted that King Ashoka was only about 200 years after the Buddha's time. This pagoda is in the Bodhi Field and next to the Bodhi tree. Since the Tang Dynasty, famous Chinese monks who traveled to the Western Regions, such as Xuanzang's Records of the Western Regions, Yijing's Dharma Returning Biography, and Faxian's Records of Buddhist Countries, have recorded the events of the Bodhi Field in detail, with every grass and tree being as detailed as it can be verified today. How could there be such a grand pagoda that has not been mentioned at all? It can be known that there was no such building at that time, and it can be known that this pagoda was built in the Song Dynasty, so tourists before the Tang Dynasty could not see it and record it. I told Dao Shi that a full photo of this pagoda and the Chinese inscription must be taken, and then the inscription must be printed and photographed to be kept on file at the Chinese Consulate, so that a case can be established for future negotiations. This is a major public case of the Chinese overseas development of cultural undertakings. I hope that the people of the country will pay attention to it. I remember that Europeans fought for a piece of Columbus's stone for a long time without a decision. In the end, the Americans bought it for 500,000 yuan and took it to the United States, which was a great joke. Another example is the hometown of the ancient poet Aesop. People from all over the world are vying for it. Today, it is said that there are three places that claim to be the birthplace of Aesop. Culture is the crown of the nation and is also an interesting contention. How much more so is this great building? I will考焉.

I discussed with Dao Shi the relationship between cultural dissemination and assimilation. The old culture of India is extremely solid, so the Buddha could not change it with softening and transmitted it to Ceylon in the south and spread it to the small countries of Nanyang, Myanmar, Siam, and Annam. Once they encountered Buddhism, they became purely Buddhist countries. In China, there is the old culture of Confucius and Lao Tzu, which can only be harmonized and not swallowed. To the east, to Korea and Japan, Buddhism is more prosperous than Confucianism. Even to Mongolia and Tibet, it is swallowed up and gone. This proves that the culture of small countries is low and the culture of the Chinese nation is complex, and it cannot be conquered by a single method. Great is the culture of China. The culture of China is harmonious with all religions, which is more harmonious and beautiful than the simplicity of small nations.

Financial Gold Market Ends with Softening

Decline of Seven Taels and Three Mace

Xiu Erfu: The situation yesterday, March 28th, was like a dream. The gold price was volatile, sometimes at 5 or 6 taels. It was difficult to guess the direction of the people's hearts. In the end, it fell by more than 7 taels. In fact, the long and short positions were facing back to back. The improvement of foreign exchange was the main reason. The prices remained unchanged, and there were various transactions on the table. Hengxingshengda was still a fierce seller, and Chenfeng Yongshunli Wanxing and others were buyers. Overseas silver markets reported slight declines, so the gold price opened high, once rising to more than 707 taels. Afterwards, it became a volatile situation. At noon, the exchange rate tended to be loose, especially with the Cantonese helping, and the selling intention was strong. The atmosphere was not good, and it turned sharply downwards. Suddenly, it had already broken the 700 tael mark, and there was almost a collapse. In the end, it was exhausted at 692 taels. This morning, the big names seemed to have a rebound trend. In the afternoon, as it was Saturday, it was closed as usual. The market situation this week was extremely volatile. The highest price was 711 taels and 5 mace, and the lowest price was 674 taels and 5 mace, a difference of 37 taels. Compared to the previous Saturday, it still fell by 2 taels.

The collapse came after the volatile situation: As soon as the May opening started in the morning, it increased by 2 taels and 5 mace to 704 taels. The silver price fell by 3/8, and the private telegram also fell by 3/16. Buyers were active, such as Yuancheng Yongda Decheng Shunli Wanxing, etc. They all came in, and British gold was also strong. May paid a settlement of 136,875. Also, the Dalian ticket Mitsui initially absorbed 1 tael and 5 mace, 4 fen and 6 li and 2.5 hao, and then 1 tael and 5 mace and 5 li, so it rose again to 707 taels. Not long after, Yuanmao Yonghengxing and others sold and fell by more than 3 taels, which was 0.035 taels. First, the announcement was not changed, and it returned from 0.0478 taels to 0.035 taels. Within the market, British gold saw a firm price, and Huabi Maixing sold June 75, and then fell to 0.015 taels. After entering, Yu Dayuanheng Zhifeng Yongtong Taichang and others bought in, and only 20 minutes later, it raised by 6 taels. At 10 o'clock, it was 707 taels and 5 mace. At this time, British gold could be seen at 75. Shortly after, Hengxingshengda and others tended to sell, and British gold was sold by Zhengjin and others in June 75, and then fell by 6 taels. After 10:30, it was 0.015 taels, and then it added more than 1 tael, which was 0.033 taels. Afterwards, it showed a weak trend again. In fact, Hengxingshengda Yuancheng Yongfu Changtianfengyong and others sold one after another. The exchange rate became more loose, and the banks ate into 875 of British gold in June. After 11:30, it was 98 taels and 78 mace. Hengxing and others still did not sell, and British gold could be settled at 875. In a moment, it fell to 93 taels and 3 mace. When the market closed at noon, it was 94 taels and 2 mace, which was a decrease of 7 taels and 3 mace compared to the previous day. It continued to suppress to 91 or 92 taels. Yarn and Cotton: Market Decline After Yarn Marking

The yarn market was stable in the morning and declined in the afternoon. However, the prices of overseas third-grade yarns were still good. Most local retailers reduced their sales due to actual sales being less favorable. With sufficient deliveries in March, they believed the upward trend was weak, so they unanimously sold off large quantities. Although there were large buyers, the overwhelming trend made it difficult to support, and the market fell by 2.3 to 4 yuan. However, a certain major merchant's intentions remained strong and did not relax at all, continuing to purchase and increase holdings. However, Japanese Lotus brand yarn continued to arrive, leading to shortages of most Japanese yarns. As for local yarn, the inventory was slightly high, but with many new sellers at a price of 70 yuan, the market price fluctuated and declined. Future movements will still depend on exchange rates and actual demand.

People's Standard Yarn Was Stable in the Morning and Lower in the Afternoon: The People's Standard Yarn market opened flat in the morning.
